48
PART 2:  STREETS AND BUILDING LINES  
 
 
CLAUSE 6: CLOSURE OF STREETS 
 
As from the date of the endorsement on the General Plan denoting the closure of a Street or a part of 
a Street as contemplated in the provisions of the Local Government Ordinance, 1939 (Ordinance 17 of 
1939), as may be amended from time to time, the Land which forms the subject of such closure, shall: 
 
(1)   be used for such purposes as the Municipality may determine, through a Land Development 
Application,  and  the  incorporation  of  the  street  into  the  Land  Use  Scheme,  read  with  the 
provisions of the LUM By-law; or 
 
(2)   subject to such condition applicable on the Land if it has been zoned and indicated on the Scheme 
Map; and 
 
(3)   it may only be used for the purpose for which it has been zoned.  
 
 
CLAUSE 7: ACCESS TO PROPERTY  
 
Entry  to  or  exit  from  any  Property,  to  or  from  a  Public  Street,  shall  be  to  the  satisfaction  of  the 
Municipality, without detracting from the generality of this Clause read with section 28(5) of the LUM 
By-law, and are subject to the following conditions: 
 
(1)   The entry to or exit from any Property shall be located, constructed, drained and maintained to 
the satisfaction of the Municipality and, if required by the Municipality such access shall be so 
constructed to include a dust-free surface and may include internal driveways, provided that: 
 
(a)   any  entrance  gate  to  a  Property,  other  than  a  Property  zoned  Residential  1  and 
Residential 5, shall be located at least six (6) metres from the boundary of the Street where 
access is taken from; and 
 
(b)   any Property zoned Residential 1 and Residential 5 may not be required to provide a dust-
free surface as contemplated above. 
 
(2)   The Municipality may prohibit the entrance to or exit from a Property to a Public Street from any 
boundary of such Property which boundary shall be indicated by the following symbol on the 
Scheme Map and is known as a Line of No Access: 
 
  
 
Provided that: 
 
(a)   the Municipality may grant Consent Use to relax or revoke such Line of No Access, subject 
to any conditions that the Municipality may impose; and 
 
(b)   the Municipality shall not relax or revoke such Line of No Access in respect of National 
Roads  or  Provincial  Roads;  until  and  unless,  the  national  or  provincial  departments 
responsible  for  the  administration  of  such  Roads  have  granted  permission  for  such 
relaxation or revocation. 
 
 
 
 

 
 
TSHWANE LAND USE SCHEME, 2024 
 
Adopted by virtue of Notice LA 652 of 2024:  08 May 2024  
Comes into operation:  01 July 2024 
                                                                             
 
 
49
CLAUSE 8: BUILDING LINES IN NEW TOWNSHIPS AND ON SUBDIVISIONS 
 
Building lines in any township established in terms of any law or in respect of Properties created by 
subdivision after the Adoption of this Scheme that are not indicated in Schedules 1 and 5 of the Scheme 
or not indicated on the Scheme Map nor indicated in Schedule 4 or in an Annexure L, shall be as 
provided for in Clauses 9 and 12. 
 
 
CLAUSE 9: STREET BUILDING LINES 
 
(1) Schedules 1 and 5 and Scheme documentation 
 
Street Building Lines relative to any existing Street, widening of an existing Street or proposed 
new  Street  shall  be  as  indicated  in  Schedules  1  and  5  and/or  on  the  Scheme  documents, 
provided that such Street Building Lines, if indicated on the aforementioned Scheme documents, 
shall override the Street Building Lines as indicated in Schedules 1 and 5. 
 
The Street Building Lines as determined in Schedules 1 and 5 shall, in the case of Apartment 
Building, Backpackers, Block of Flats and Hotel, be calculated in addition to the widths of any 
servitude of right-of way, provided that: 
 
(a)   where  Street  Building  Lines  are  not  specified  in  Schedules  1  and  5  or  on  the 
aforementioned  Scheme  documents  or  Site  Development  Plan,  the  following  shall  be 
applicable  to  all  Buildings,  but  excluding  a  garage  or  carport  on  a  Property  zoned 
Residential 1, subject to Subclauses (1)(b), (c) and (d), (2), (3) and (4): 
 
(i)    Residential 5 zoned Properties: one (1) metre. 
 
(ii)    Agricultural and Undetermined zoned Properties: ten (10) metres. 
 
(iii)   All other Use Zones: two (2) metres; 
 
(b)   nothing contained in Clause 9 shall prevent the Municipality from determining a Street 
Building Line, to its satisfaction, where the Street Building Line is not indicated on the 
Scheme documents or in these clauses; 
 
(c)   an additional minimum distance of 3,5 metres shall be imposed on the Street Building Line 
where Blocks of Flats are erected with Habitable Rooms on the Ground Floor on Business 
1 or Business 2 zoned Properties; and 
 
(d)   a Property zoned Residential 1 located on a corner where two or more Streets intersect, 
where the Street Building Line is more than 3,5 metres, the Municipality may, on any one 
of the Street Boundaries, reduce such Street Building Line to 3,5 metres. 
 
(2)   Building restriction and relaxation 
 
Buildings shall not be erected on the  Land between  the Street Building Line and the  Street 
Boundary, provided that the Municipality may grant Permission to relax any such Street Building 
Line. 
 
(3)   Use Zones Business 1, Business 2, Business 3 and Business 4 
 
In Use Zones Business 1, Business 2, Business 3 and Business 4, parking of vehicles shall be 
permitted  in  the  area  between  the  Street  Building  Line  and  the  Street  Boundary  and  the 
Municipality  may  grant  Permission to  use the aforementioned  area  or  part  thereof  for  other 
purposes, provided that: 
 

 
 
TSHWANE LAND USE SCHEME, 2024 
 
Adopted by virtue of Notice LA 652 of 2024:  08 May 2024  
Comes into operation:  01 July 2024 
                                                                             
 
 
50
(a)   the area may be used for serving and consuming of meals and refreshments only if used 
in conjunction with a Place of Refreshment and subject to an approved Site Development 
Plan; 
 
(b)   the area shall, if used as permitted in the Subclause (3)(a), be included in the calculation 
of Floor Area Ratio and Coverage; 
 
(c)   the area shall not be used for the storage of goods or merchandise, or for advertisement;  
 
(d)   should the Municipality require additional Land for street widening, any Building shall be 
removed at no cost to the Municipality and the Municipality shall not be liable for any 
compensation other than for the Land so acquired; and 
 
(e)   such Land may be used for purposes of provision of Open Space and included in the 
contributions of Open Space as may be determined by the Municipality. 
 
(4)   Basements 
 
Basements  shall  not  be  permitted  in  the  area  between  the  Street  Boundary  and  the  Street 
Building Line, except with the Permission of the Municipality. 
 
 
CLAUSE 10: CANOPIES OVER STREET BUILDING LINES 
 
(1)   The Municipality may grant Permission for Canopies to project over the Street Building Line. 
 
(2)   Canopies of Filling Stations and Public Garages, excluding the columns or support structures 
thereof, may encroach over the Street Building Line by a maximum of three (3) metres. The 
Municipality may grant Permission to relax the distance of the projection of the Canopies over 
the Street Building Line to a further distance than three (3) metres, provided that a Canopy may 
not extend over the boundary of the Property onto the road reserve or Street. 
 
 
CLAUSE 11: LAND FOR STREET WIDENING 
 
(1)   The Municipality may require Land along any Street Boundary of a Property for purposes of 
widening a Street, provided that: 
 
(a)   if acquired by the Municipality for that purpose the zoning of that part of the Property shall 
automatically be zoned as “Existing Streets”;  
 
(b)   the land use rights of the Property or part of the Property that is the subject of a street 
widening shall not, with the reduction of the area of the Property for the widening of the 
Street, constitute a contravention of the land use rights of the Property so reduced;  
 
(c)   the Municipality for purposes of widening the Street, shall amend the Scheme in terms of 
section 13 of the LUM By-law, to indicate the land use rights as it will apply to the Property 
forming  the  subject  of  the  widening  and  the  part  of  the  Property  that  constitutes  the 
widening; and 
 
(d)   Clause 20(4) shall be applicable to Properties zoned Residential 1. 
 
(2)   When Land is proclaimed or vested in terms of any legislation for purposes of the widening of 
National Roads and Provincial Roads required along a Street Boundary of or over a Property 
for purposes of acquiring such Land for the widening of National Roads and Provincial Roads, 
the following shall be applicable: 
 

 
 
TSHWANE LAND USE SCHEME, 2024 
 
Adopted by virtue of Notice LA 652 of 2024:  08 May 2024  
Comes into operation:  01 July 2024 
                                                                             
 
 
51
(a)   if such Land is legally acquired through the registration thereof in the name of the relevant 
organs  of  state  or  national  or  provincial  owned  entities,  the  national  or  provincial 
departments shall consider and provide information on the impact of the said acquisition 
and registration on the Zoning, land use rights and controls applicable to the remaining 
part of the Property from which it will be separated/deducted; 
 
(b)   if the Municipality upon perusal of such impact and information is satisfied that the land 
use rights, as a result of the acquisition for the widening of the National Roads or Provincial 
Roads, can  be  exercised on the that part  of the Property, the portion of the  Property 
acquired by the relevant organ of state shall automatically be zoned as Existing Streets; 
 
(c)   the Municipality may determine that the land use rights of the Property that is the subject 
of a street widening shall not, with the reduction of the area of the Property for the widening 
of the National Roads and Provincial Roads constitute a contravention of the land use 
rights of the Property, provided that the Municipality, for purposes of widening the National 
Roads and Provincial Roads, shall amend the Scheme in terms of section 13 of the LUM 
By-law, to indicate the land use rights as it will apply; 
 
(d)   Clause 20(4) shall be applicable to Properties zoned Residential 1; and  
 
(e)   a Land Development Application in terms of section 16(16) or other provisions of the 
LUM By-law may be required as may be determined by the Municipality. 
 
 
CLAUSE 12: SIDE BUILDING LINES AND REAR BUILDING LINES  
 
(1) Table A: Side Building Lines and Rear Building Lines 
 
Subject to any other provision of this Scheme, Buildings or any alteration, extension or addition 
to an existing Building shall not project over or encroach the Side Building Line and Rear Building 
Line as specified in Table A, provided that if a Land Development Application for the increase in 
Height is approved by the Municipality, the width of the Side Building Line and Rear Building Line 
may  be  increased  as  part  of  the  Land  Development  Application  to  the  satisfaction  of  the 
Municipality. 
 
(2) Additional provisions to Subclause (1) and Table A or any By-laws 
 
Notwithstanding the provisions of Subclause (1) and Table A or any By-laws: 
 
(a)   any open porch, step, gate, fence, wall or Physical Barrier not exceeding 2,1 metres in 
height measured from Natural Ground Level, may encroach on any Side Building Line and 
Rear Building Line; and 
 
(b)   balconies of Apartment Buildings, Block of Flats and Dwelling Units,  may project to a 
maximum distance of 0,70 metres over the Side Building Line and Rear Building Line, 
provided that: 
 
(i)    such balconies are single units and not enclosed; and 
 
(ii)    the aggregate length of all such balconies shall not exceed 50% of the length of the 
Building. 
 
(c)   a single Storey garage, carport, shelter; laundry, private swimming pool, change room for 
a private swimming pool, tennis court, squash court or storeroom may be erected on any 
area between the Side Building Line and Side Boundary, and the Rear Building Line and 
Rear Boundary, excluding any Buildings that are adjacent to a Street Boundary, provided 
that: 

 
 
TSHWANE LAND USE SCHEME, 2024 
 
Adopted by virtue of Notice LA 652 of 2024:  08 May 2024  
Comes into operation:  01 July 2024 
                                                                             
 
 
52
 
(i)    the position thereof is not detrimental to the amenities of the adjoining Property(ies);  
 
(ii)    the Height of such Building above Natural Ground Level on the Side Boundary or 
Rear Boundary shall not exceed three (3) metres; 
 
(iii)   the external face of the boundary wall shall be face brick, unless an alternative 
durable finish is agreed to in writing by the Owner(s) of the adjoining Property(ies) 
and  such  boundary  wall  shall  have  a  firewall  of  maximum  500  mm  above  the 
maximum Height specified in proviso (ii) above; 
 
(iv)   any carport, shelter, which is built on any boundary other than a Street Boundary, 
shall be completely open on two sides, and the length thereof shall not exceed 7,50 
metres without the Permission of the Municipality; and 
 
(v)   it shall be erected on or directly against the Side Boundary or Rear Boundary or at 
least one (1) metre from the said boundary. 
 
(d)   the Municipality may grant Permission for: 
 
(i)    any Building, including a Basement, to encroach on any of the Side Building Lines 
and Rear Building Lines specified in Table A; 
 
(ii)    any other Building designed and used exclusively as a doll's house, poultry-house, 
aviary, pigeon loft, potting-shed, tool-shed, coal-shed, cycle-shed, summer-house, 
pump-house, water tank, Guard House, Reservoir or dog kennel to be erected in 
the area between the Side Building Line and Side Boundary, and the Rear Building 
Line and Rear Boundary, provided it is screened off behind a wall of at least two (2) 
metres high and not visible from a Street and adjacent Properties and it shall not be 
used for residential purposes or as a Home Enterprise; and 
 
(iii)   the maximum Height of three (3) metres, as required by Subclause (2)(c)(ii), and the 
maximum  height  of  2,1  metres  of  a  wall  or  Physical  Barrier,  as  required  by 
Subclause (2)(a), to be exceeded. 
 
(3) Southern boundaries in Table A 
 
(a)   The reference to southern boundaries in Table A shall mean the boundaries of a Property, 
which approximate the southern-most boundary(ies) of such Property. 
 
(b)   The provisions of Subclause (2) above shall not apply to the southern boundary of the 
Property except for Subclause (2)(d) relating to relaxation, which relaxation shall not be to 
a Building Line less than two (2) metres, provided that for Use Zone 5, Residential 5, where 
the Building Line is specified as one (1) metre, it shall not be relaxed. 
 
(c)   Where special circumstances exist, as may be determined by the Municipality, due to the 
orientation, location  and layout of Existing  Buildings  on the  Property, or  the particular 
shape of a Property, the Municipality may grant Permission to use the Building Restriction 
Area on the southern boundary of a Property as provided for in Subclause (2) above. 
 
(4) Building Restriction Area on southern boundaries 
 
The Building Restriction Area on southern boundaries shall be maintained to prevent winter over 
shadowing  onto  the  adjacent  Properties,  except  where  special  circumstances  will  allow  an 
encroachment with Permission of the Municipality, read with Subclause (3)(c) but in all instances 
excludes where such boundaries that are common boundaries with a Street or Road. 
  

 
 
TSHWANE LAND USE SCHEME, 2024 
 
Adopted by virtue of Notice LA 652 of 2024:  08 May 2024  
Comes into operation:  01 July 2024

54
 
(5)   Consolidation of Properties 
 
If two (2) or more Properties are consolidated, the Side Building Line and Rear Building Line 
required in terms of this Scheme in respect of the former common boundary shall fall away, 
provided further that the provisions of this Subclause shall mutatis mutandis also apply if two (2) 
or more Properties are Notarially Tied. 
 
(6) Servitudes, engineering services and Building Restriction Area 
 
(a)   A Land Development Application for relaxation of a Building Restriction Area shall indicate 
servitudes and engineering services where applicable. 
 
(b)   A servitude which is duly registered against the title deed of a Property, as the servient 
tenement or an ex lege servitude as contemplated in Clause 18 to this Scheme, shall prevail 
over any Building Restriction Area and such Building Restriction Area shall not be relaxed 
beyond the servitude line, unless such servitude has been cancelled and de-registered.

55
PART 3:  USE OF LAND AND BUILDINGS 
 
 
CLAUSE 13: MIXED USE OF BUILDINGS 
 
Where a Building is used or a proposed Building is designed for more than one (1) use, it shall be 
deemed for the purpose of Clauses 14, 25, 26 and 27 hereof, to be used or designed partly for each of 
these uses, except that for the purposes of the other provisions of this part of the Scheme, it shall be 
deemed to be used or designed for its predominant use and the Municipality shall, on application to 
erect the Building, determine by its sole discretion which is the predominant use. 
 
 
CLAUSE 14: USE OF LAND AND BUILDINGS 
 
(1) Proposed Streets and Widening of existing Streets 
 
Proposed Streets and Widening of existing Streets as specified in Table B shall not be deemed 
to be Streets until such Streets or any portions thereof fall within a township which may be 
established, or these are proclaimed as Streets or become vested in the Municipality for that 
purpose in terms of any other law, provided that, if a township is established or subdivision is 
approved, the position of the aforementioned Streets may be amended to align with the layout of 
the township or subdivision. 
 
(2) Execution of works by the Municipality 
 
Where  the  Municipality  has  acquired,  either  by  agreement,  or  by  any  other  legal  means  or 
expropriation,  any  Land  together  with  Buildings,  zoned  in  terms  of  Table B  hereof,  the 
Municipality may execute thereon such works as may be required for or be incidental to the 
purpose for which the Land was acquired or expropriated, is zoned and/or for the installation of 
Municipal services and works. 
 
(3) Table B 
 
Table B indicates different categories of land use Zoning and for each of these Use Zones the 
purposes in: 
 
Column (3), for which Buildings may be erected and used or Land used (also known as primary 
land uses); 
 
Column (4), for which Buildings may be erected and used or Land used only with the Consent 
Use of the Municipality; and 
 
Column (5), for which Buildings may not be erected and used, nor Land used. 
 
 
REFER TO TABLE B ON PAGES 58 UP TO AND INCLUDING 77 
 
(4) Contraventions 
 
Land, Buildings or part thereof shall not be used for a purpose other than for which is provided 
for in this Scheme, unless such Building has been altered for any new use to the satisfaction of 
the Municipality, read with section 26 of the Act. 
 
 

 
 
TSHWANE LAND USE SCHEME, 2024 
 
Adopted by virtue of Notice LA 652 of 2024:  08 May 2024  
Comes into operation:  01 July 2024 
                                                                             
 
 
56
(5) Existing Buildings and new Buildings 
 
The expression "may be erected and used" means the use in a new Building or the conversion 
of an existing Building for that use, whether it requires the structural alteration thereof or not. 
 
(6) Specific uses always subject to the Municipality’s consent in terms of Clause 16 
 
(a)   Land  in  any  Use  Zone  used  for  the  purpose  of  refuse  or  rubbish  tipping,  or  sewage 
disposal. 
 
(b)   Land in any Use Zone used for the removal of soil, sand, clay, gravel or stone for the sale, 
distribution or further processing thereof, for financial gain. 
 
(c)   Land in Use Zones 1, 2, 3, 4 and 5 used for the parking of commercial vehicles, excluding 
vehicles as described in Schedule 9, Part A, Condition (3)(d). 
 
(d)   The manufacturing of products of commercial value from soil, sand, clay, gravel or stone 
on  the  Land  where  these  materials  are  extracted,  on  condition  that  a  guarantee  is 
submitted to the effect that the Land will be restored in accordance with the conditions 
imposed. 
 
(7) Noxious Industries subject to the Municipality’s consent in terms of Clause 16 
 
The Municipality may grant consent in terms of Clause 16 for the erection and use of Buildings 
for Noxious Industries in Use Zone 10, Industrial 1, provided that: 
 
(a)   a certificate shall be issued by the Municipality’s Health Officer in consultation with the 
Inspector of Factories, declaring that the processes of such Noxious Industry as listed in 
Schedule 8, shall not have a negative impact on neighbouring Properties; 
 
(b)   this certificate mentioned in Subclause (a) may impose conditions that if land treatment of 
such matters is proposed, the nature, slope and area of the Land relative to dwellings, 
streams or water courses, shall be to the satisfaction of the Municipality; and  
 
(c)   the  Municipality’s  Health  Officer  may  impose  additional  conditions  relating  to  such 
certification as mentioned in Subclause (a). 
 
(8) Use of any Land for Public Service Infrastructure 
Notwithstanding any provision in this Scheme read with Table B contained herein, any Land and 
Building may be used for Public Service Infrastructure or if classified as such by the Municipality 
in terms of paragraph 1(j) of the definition of Public Service Infrastructure, provided that: 
 
(a)   the Municipality may determine whether: 
 
(i)    a Permission application needs to be submitted;  
 
(ii)   public participation may be required read with section 16(16) of the LUM By-law; 
 
(b)   the Municipality shall for purposes of granting such Permissions consider the impact of the 
Public Service Infrastructure on the land use rights of the Property on which it is required 
and for that purpose, impose any conditions it deems expedient to ensure that the land 
use rights of the Property on which the Public Service Infrastructure will be constructed 
and or used, shall comply with the provisions of this Scheme, including the replacement of 
an Amendment Scheme in terms of section 13 of the LUM By-law; and 
 
 

 
 
TSHWANE LAND USE SCHEME, 2024 
 
Adopted by virtue of Notice LA 652 of 2024:  08 May 2024  
Comes into operation:  01 July 2024 
                                                                             
 
 
57
(c) Permission granted in terms of Subclause 14(8)(a)(i) for Public Service Infrastructure shall 
not lapse and may be retained with the rezoning of any Property or where any township 
establishment  has  been  Adopted  except,  where  such  application  mentions  that  the 
Permission should not be retained as part of the new land uses applied for.  
 
(9) Title Deed, adopted Annexure L, Consent Use and Deed of Grant referring to “business” 
or “business purpose” 
 
(a)   Any Building or Land used in such a way that it will or is intended to generate income from 
the sale of goods or provision of services other than the renting of Buildings for residential 
purposes, shall be regarded as a business for the purposes of the meaning of a business 
where it is stated in a condition in any Title Deed of a Property, and such condition in the 
Title Deed shall be deemed to be restrictive.  
 
(b)   Where it is referred to in documents such as an Annexure L, Consent Use, Deed of Grant 
as “business purpose” then it means Land and Buildings used for Business Building, Place 
of Amusement, Place of Refreshment, Retail Industry, Shop and Vehicle Sales Mart or 
other business enterprises for financial gain, as contemplated in the Scheme. 
 
(c)   Clause 38 shall be applicable. 
 
(10) One (1) Additional Dwelling House  
 
Notwithstanding any stipulation in this Scheme, the Municipality may grant Permission for the 
erection of one (1) Additional Dwelling House on a Property zoned Residential 1, Agricultural or 
Undetermined, provided that: 
 
(a)   Clause 15, Clause 18(6), Clause 19 and Clause 20(2) shall be applicable. 
 
(b)   Properties in areas as contemplated in Schedules 11, 12, 13 and 14 shall be excluded 
from the provision of this Subclause. 
 
(c)   This Subclause (10) is also applicable to a Property zoned Residential 1 with a Density of 
“One Dwelling House per Erf”. 
 
(d)   This Subclause (10) is also applicable to a Property zoned Residential 1 with a specified 
Minimum Erf Size as indicated in Schedule 6, i.e., the Electronic Zoning Database. 
 
(11) Children’s playground 
 
(a)   The Owner of any Property in any Use Zone that is used for Dwelling Units registered as 
a sectional title scheme and Blocks of Flats, shall provide, develop and maintain children’s 
playground on the Property with the requirement of four (4) m² per Dwelling Unit with a 
minimum of 50 m² on the Property, provided that the Municipality may grant Permission to 
reduce the area. 
 
(b)   The areas in Subclause (a) shall not be regarded as the provision of Open Space as 
contemplated in section 46 of the LUM By-law. 
 
(c)   Properties zoned Residential 1 and Residential 5 shall be excluded. 
 
(12) Agricultural Holdings 
 
The Municipality may, notwithstanding anything to the contrary contained in the provisions of this 
Scheme, give Permission for any use if such Permission may be granted in terms of a condition 
of a Title Deed of any Agricultural Holding or may be granted in terms of the Agricultural Holdings 
(Transvaal) Registration Act, 1919 (Act 22 of 1919) on any Agricultural Holding,  provided that 

 
 
TSHWANE LAND USE SCHEME, 2024 
 
Adopted by virtue of Notice LA 652 of 2024:  08 May 2024  
Comes into operation:  01 July 2024 
                                                                             
 
 
58
any Permission granted, shall not grant Permission or have the result of any Property or a portion, 
section or unit thereof being alienated to more than one (1) Person.   
 
(13) Consent Use(s) and Permission(s) on farm portions or Agricultural Holdings 
 
Multiple  Consent  Uses  and/or  a  Consent  Use  and  Permission  cannot  be  approved  on  an 
Agricultural Holding or a Farm Portion if such approvals will constitute an Illegal Township, read 
with the provisions of the LUM By-law.

CLAUSE 15: PERMISSION OF THE MUNICIPALITY 
 
(1)   An Applicant may apply to the Municipality for Permission to use Land and Buildings or to relax 
certain conditions provided for in this Scheme, its Schedules and Annexures L and other Scheme 
documents, where such Permission is explicitly provided for in this Scheme, subject to a Land 
Development Application procedure as prescribed in the LUM By-law.   
 
(2)    An Applicant may apply for the amendment of a Permission as contemplated in Subclause (1) 
and the Municipality may grant its Permission to amend the conditions of approval of an Adopted 
Permission and Consent Use of the Municipality, provided this amendment does not materially 
and substantially change the rights and conditions approved and further provided that, there 
were no objections to the initial application, subject to the payment of a prescribed fee. 
 
 
CLAUSE 16: CONSENT OF THE MUNICIPALITY 
 
(1) Application procedure 
 
An Applicant may apply to the Municipality for consent to use Land and Buildings or to relax 
certain conditions provided for in this Scheme, its Schedules and Annexures L and other Scheme 
documents  where  such  consent  is  explicitly  provided  for  in  this  Scheme,  subject  to  a  Land 
Development Application procedure as prescribed in the LUM By-law.  
 
 

 
 
TSHWANE LAND USE SCHEME, 2024 
 
Adopted by virtue of Notice LA 652 of 2024:  08 May 2024  
Comes into operation:  01 July 2024 
                                                                             
 
 
78
(2) Consent Use types 
 
An Applicant may apply to the Municipality for consent - 
 
(a)   where Buildings may be erected and used or Land used in Use Zone 1 up to and including 
Use Zone 28, as set out in Column (4) of Table B; 
 
(b)   for the  erection of a Building to  a Height greater than that  permitted as prescribed  in 
Clause 26; 
 
(c)   for land uses as contemplated in Clause 14 and Schedule 9; 
 
(d)   for any other provision in this Scheme or in a Scheme document not provided for in Clauses 
15 or 16(1), which requires the consent or approval of the local authority or Municipality or 
City Council or administrator; and 
 
(e)   for the Mining of Land in any Use Zone in terms of the Mineral and Petroleum Resources 
Development Act, 2002 (Act 28 of 2002) as provided for in Schedule 17. 
 
 
CLAUSE 17: TEMPORARY USE AND OCCASIONAL USE 
 
(1) Temporary Use 
 
Notwithstanding any provision to the contrary contained in this Scheme the Municipality may 
grant Permission for the Temporary Use of any Building or Land within any Use Zone for any of 
the following: 
 
(a)   The erection and use of temporary Buildings or the use of Existing Buildings or Properties 
for site offices, store rooms, Workshops or such other uses that are in the opinion of the 
Municipality necessary for the erection of any permanent Building on the Property or the 
installation of engineering services, which shall be to the satisfaction of the Municipality, 
provided  that  such Permission  which  shall  lapse,  ipso  facto,  on  completion  of  the 
permanent Building or the completion of the engineering contract; and 
 
(b)   Uses such as, but not limited to, circuses, Flea Market, Parking Site, Place of Amusement, 
Place of Public Worship, public gatherings or meetings, Social Halls, street vendors and 
any other use which the Municipality in the interest of the community may approve, subject 
to the following:  
 
(i)    The Municipality, may impose any conditions which it may deem necessary;  
 
(ii)    the Permission may be withdrawn after 30 days written notice to the Applicant if any 
conditions of the Permission are not complied with or where malpractice occurs, or 
the amenity of the area is prejudiced; 
 
(iii)   the Permission shall expire 3 months from the date on which the Permission was 
granted unless the Municipality extends it in writing for a further period not exceeding 
3 months, after receiving a written request from the Applicant; and 
 
(iv)   any period longer than 6 months, shall be regarded as an intention of permanent 
use and shall be subject to a Land Development Application and if not removed after 
the expiry of the date shall be regarded as a contravention, irrespective of whether 
a Land Development Application has been submitted or not. 
 

 
 
TSHWANE LAND USE SCHEME, 2024 
 
Adopted by virtue of Notice LA 652 of 2024:  08 May 2024  
Comes into operation:  01 July 2024 
                                                                             
 
 
79
(c)   Permission shall not be applicable for site offices adjacent to National Roads or Provincial 
Roads for purposes of the upgrading or building of such National Roads or Provincial 
Roads. 
 
(2) Occasional Use 
 
Without detracting from any powers of the Municipality authorised in terms of any other law or 
any provision of this Scheme, nothing in Clauses 14(3) or 16 of this Scheme shall be interpreted 
and regarded as having granted powers to the Municipality to prohibit or restrict the Occasional 
Use of a Place of Public Worship, Place of Instruction or Institution as a Place of Amusement or 
Social Hall.

PART 4:  DEVELOPMENT CONDITIONS 
 
 
CLAUSE 18: GENERAL CONDITIONS APPLICABLE TO ALL PROPERTIES AND STREETS 
 
(1) Conditions applicable to all Properties 
 
(a) Conditions applicable to all Erven 
 
(i)    Servitudes for Municipal Infrastructure Services 
 
(aa)  A servitude two (2) metres wide in favour of the Municipality shall be provided 
for Municipal Infrastructure Services along any boundary, other than a Street 
Boundary, where such services are installed or planned to be installed. 
 
(bb)  A Building or part of its foundations may not be erected in the servitude area 
referred to in the Subclause (1)(a)(i)(aa) and trees with a potentially large root 
system may not be planted within the aforementioned servitude area or within 
two (2) metres thereof except with the Permission of the Municipality.  
 
(cc)   The Municipality shall be entitled to reasonable access to the Land adjoining 
the servitude area referred to in Subclause (1)(a)(i)(aa) for the construction, 
maintenance  or  removal  of  such  services  as  the  Municipality  deems 
necessary. The Municipality shall be entitled to deposit temporarily on the 
aforementioned Land, material that may be excavated during the course of 
such  activities,  subject  to  any  damage  caused  being  rectified  by  the 
Municipality at its cost. 
 
(ii)    Provisions for storm water  
 
(aa)  The Owner is bound and obliged to receive storm water that naturally drains 
onto the Erf from Land lying on a higher level. 
 
(bb)  The Owner of a higher lying Erf may not concentrate the flow of storm water 
on a lower lying Erf. 
 
(cc)   If it is not possible to prevent the concentrated discharge of storm water from 
any higher lying Erf onto a lower lying Erf, or for storm water to be drained 
from any high lying Erf directly to a Public Street, the Owner of any lower lying 
Erf shall be obliged to accept and permit the passage of such storm water to 
be discharged. 
 
(dd)  The Owner of such high lying Erf from which the storm water is discharged, 
over the lower lying Erf, shall be liable for the cost of any pipeline or drain 
which the Owner of such lower lying Erf may find necessary for the purpose 
of conducting such storm water discharge. 
 
(ee)  Any restrictive conditions contained in a title deed of any Erf, relating to these 
Subclauses (1)(a)(ii)(aa) up to and including (1)(a)(ii)(dd) above, shall not be 
removed or amended by virtue of a land development application. 
 
(iii)   Bricks, tiles or earthenware pipes or other similar articles may not be manufactured, 
unless the Zoning permits such activities. 
 

 
 
TSHWANE LAND USE SCHEME, 2024 
 
Adopted by virtue of Notice LA 652 of 2024:  08 May 2024  
Comes into operation:  01 July 2024 
                                                                             
 
 
81
(iv)   Material may not be excavated from any Erf except to prepare the Erf for building 
purposes. 
 
(v)   Animals as defined in the By-laws for Keeping of Animals, Birds and Poultry and to 
Businesses involving the Keeping of Animals, Birds, Poultry and Pets, 2017, as may 
be  amended  from  time  to  time,  may  not  be  kept  on  any  Erf  except  with  the 
Permission of the Municipality, unless the Zoning permits such activities. 
 
(vi)   Wells or boreholes may not be sunk on any Erf except with the Permission of the 
Municipality and subject to such conditions as the Municipality may impose. 
 
(vii)   Main Buildings shall be erected and completed simultaneously with or before the 
erection of the Outbuildings. 
 
(b) Conditions  applicable  to  residential  development  or  similar  development  on 
farmland or Agricultural Holdings 
 
The conditions contemplated in Subclauses (1)(a)(i) up to and including (1)(a)(vii) shall 
also be applicable on any Property that is being used in a manner that in the opinion of the 
Municipality, can be regarded as being used predominantly for residential development or 
purposes or similar development on farmland or Agricultural Holdings, other than it being 
used for bona fide agricultural use, and if so regarded shall not in any manner be construed 
as having been granted residential land use rights.  
 
(2) Conditions applicable in terms of Schedule 5 
 
Certain townships and Erven are subject to further conditions as set out in Schedule 5. 
 
(3) Physical Barriers and screen walls 
 
(a)   The Municipality may require that a screen wall of at least two (2) metres high be erected 
on one or more boundaries or elsewhere on all Properties except Properties in Use Zones 
Residential 1 and Residential 5. 
 
(b)   If a Property is fenced or walled in by any means whatsoever, such fence or wall shall be 
to the satisfaction of the Municipality. 
 
(4) Maintenance of Property 
 
(a)   Every Owner and Occupant of a Property is responsible  for the maintenance  of such 
Property, including the improvements on it as well as the garden, to the satisfaction of the 
Municipality.  
 
(b)   The refuse areas where rubbish or waste is temporarily stored before it is removed, shall 
be properly screened from the Street and adjacent Properties and regularly removed to 
the satisfaction of the Municipality. 
 
(5) Informal trade on Streets 
 
Informal  trade  shall  not  be  conducted  on  any  Street  or  Road  within  the  jurisdiction  of  the 
Municipality, without the Permission of the  Municipality and subject to its By-laws and other 
legislation regulating such trade.  
 
(6) Provisions for septic tanks and french drains 
 
(a)   Septic tanks and french drains shall be located at least 50 metres from any borehole being 
used for drinking water. 

 
 
TSHWANE LAND USE SCHEME, 2024 
 
Adopted by virtue of Notice LA 652 of 2024:  08 May 2024  
Comes into operation:  01 July 2024 
                                                                             
 
 
82
 
(b)   The  design  and  construction  of  septic  tanks  and  french  drains  shall  comply  with  the 
Municipality’s requirements. 
 
(c)   Septic tanks and french drains shall not be installed, constructed or placed without the 
Permission of the Municipality. 
 
(7) By-laws of the Municipality and other relevant legislation  
 
(a)   Health and safety standards shall be applicable to all Land and Buildings. The Owners and 
Occupants of such Land and Buildings shall comply with the relevant standards as well as 
any By-laws enforced by the Municipality, provided that in the event of conflict between 
the provisions of the Scheme and a By-law the provisions of the Scheme shall prevail.  
 
(b)   All relevant requirements specified in any other legislation applicable shall be complied 
with prior to final approval of a Land Development Application in terms of this Scheme and 
the LUM By-Law, or before any land use is exercised in terms of the provisions of this 
Scheme. 
 
(8) Airport, Airfield and Helipad conditions 
 
(a)   Applicants  intending  to  apply  for  any  Land  Development  Application  in  terms  of  this 
Scheme and the LUM By-Law, must take cognisance of the restrictions on development 
in the vicinity of the landing and take-off areas of an Airport and Airfield as laid down in the 
South African Civil Aviation Act, 2009 (Act 13 of 2009) as may be amended from time to 
time, and its Regulations. 
 
(b)   Micro light aircraft, helicopters and other forms of air transport shall not be parked, stored, 
driven or flown to or from any Property in Use Zones 1, 2, 3, 4, 5, 6, 7, 8, 9, 13, 14, 18, 20, 
21, 22, 23 and 26 of Table B, provided that subject to Clause 16, the Municipality may 
grant its consent for the aforementioned uses on Properties in Use Zones 10, 11, 12, 15, 
16, 17, 19, 25 and 27 of Table B. 
 
(9) Air Rights, Streets, National Roads and Provincial Roads 
 
(a)   Any Land Development Application for Air Rights that spans across a National Roads or 
Provincial Roads or Street, shall be subject to the support of the relevant authorities. 
 
(b)   The approval of the Land Development Application referred to in Subclause (9)(a) shall 
indicate the maximum height above the road and street level, the specific land uses and 
the area expressed in square metres. 
 
(c)   Where a National Road or Provincial Road or Street does not have a Property description 
or where a Property description is available, and an Annexure L is not applicable and the 
Zoning is Existing Street, the development controls shall be the following: 
 
(i)    FAR: Not applicable; 
 
(ii)    Height: Clause 26, Height Zone 5 of Table D; and 
 
(iii)   Coverage: Not applicable. 
 
(d)   Where  an  Annexure  L  is  applicable,  the  development  controls  as  set  out  in  such  an 
Annexure L shall prevail, but where the Annexure L has no reference to any particular 
development controls, then the development controls of Subclause (9)(c) shall apply. 
 
 

 
 
TSHWANE LAND USE SCHEME, 2024 
 
Adopted by virtue of Notice LA 652 of 2024:  08 May 2024  
Comes into operation:  01 July 2024 
                                                                             
 
 
83
(10) Provision of engineering services 
 
(a)   Every  Property  developed  in  terms  of  any  Land  Development  Application  submitted, 
approved  or  Adopted  in  terms  of  this  Scheme,  and  any  applicable  planning  and 
development  legislation,  shall  be  provided  with  such  engineering  services,  as  the 
Municipality may deem necessary for the proper development of the Property and include 
Private Infrastructure Services developed or provided by the Owner of such Property read 
with the LUM By-law. 
 
(b)   The  Owner(s)  of  any  Property(ies),  which  are  the  subject  of  a  Land  Development 
Application in terms of any applicable planning and development legislation, shall at their 
costs and to the satisfaction of the Municipality, design, provide and construct all internal 
engineering services whether public or private engineering services, whether it shall be 
taken over by the Municipality or not, with reference to the engineering services related to 
the particular application, to the satisfaction of the Municipality. 
 
(c)   The  Owner(s)  shall,  within  such  period  as  the  Municipality  may  determine,  fulfil  their 
obligations  in  respect  of  all  internal  and  external  engineering  services,  such  as  the 
provision of water and sanitary services, as well as the construction of Streets and storm 
water drainage and the installation of systems therefore, as determined by the Municipality, 
which requirements shall be provided to the Applicant and as agreed upon between the 
Applicant(s) and the Municipality.  
 
(d)   For the purpose of the Scheme, any engineering services or Open Space requirements 
shall be reflected as part of the Land Development Application and shall be taken up in the 
Scheme, Amendment Scheme or decision, as conditions whichever is applicable. 
 
(e)   Where  engineering  services  construction  and  upgrades  are  required  on  external 
engineering services as defined in terms of the LUM By-law, or other applicable legislation, 
as may be amended from time to time, the Municipality may require that: 
 
(i)    at the expense of the Applicant a service scheme report be prepared by a registered 
professional engineer, addressing the provision of Streets and storm water for a 
Land  Development  Application,  including  storm  water  management  on  site 
attenuation,  to  the  satisfaction  of  the  Municipality  and  may  be  required  to  be 
submitted for consideration and approval; and 
 
(ii)    the requirements for engineering services shall be incorporated into an application 
in terms of any legislation for consideration, including the determination of conditions 
applicable, to a Land Development Application. 
 
(f)    Without  derogating  from  any  specific  engineering  services  requirements  or  any  Land 
Development  Application,  all  engineering  services  constructed  as  a  result  of  a  Land 
Development  Application  either  by  the  Property  Owner  or  the  Municipality,  shall  be 
protected by means of servitudes in favour of the Municipality, which servitudes shall be 
provided  free  of  cost  and  compensation,  prior  to  the  exercising  of  any  land  use  or 
development rights read with the LUM By-law. 
 
(g)   If  and  when  required,  engineering  services  agreements  may  be  entered  into  by  the 
Municipality  and  the  Applicant  with  regard  to  the  provision  of  engineering  services, 
engineering contributions/development charges, guarantees or any applicable engineering 
terms and conditions read with the LUM By-law. 
 
(h)   The 1:50 and 1:100 year flood line certification, by a Professional Engineer, in respect of 
any  application  on  any  Property  within  the  jurisdiction  of  the  Municipality,  as  may  be 
determined by the Municipality, shall be obtained and indicated on the diagrams or layout 

 
 
TSHWANE LAND USE SCHEME, 2024 
 
Adopted by virtue of Notice LA 652 of 2024:  08 May 2024  
Comes into operation:  01 July 2024 
                                                                             
 
 
84
plans or any relevant documentation read with the Water Services Act, 1997 (Act 108 of 
1997), as may be amended from time to time.  
 
(i)    Where the Municipality is not the bulk supplier of electricity to a Property, the Property 
Owner shall make the necessary arrangements with ESKOM, the licensed supplier of 
electricity to the Property, to the satisfaction of the Municipality. 
 
(j)    Any noise generated from a Building, other than construction noise, shall comply with the 
noise zone criteria and acoustical screening requirements of the Municipality. 
 
(11) Non-profit companies and homeowners- or landowners- or residents association 
 
(a)   Access Control and a Guard House may be erected on the part indicated as a Private 
Street or servitude of right of way, to the satisfaction of the Municipality, provided it shall 
be indicated on a Site Development Plan contemplated in Clause 31 and approved by the 
Municipality. 
 
(b)   A Private Street, whether by means of a portion of an Erf or Erf or right of way servitude is 
created for any Land Development Application contemplated in (a) above, shall comply 
with the provisions of section 34 of the LUM By-law read with Schedule 19 thereof. 
 
(c)   The Municipality may for purposes of the management and maintenance of any private 
access  arrangements  or  engineering  services  contemplated  herein,  determine  the 
conditions related thereto, including but not limited to the establishment of a non-profit 
company or other entity, the conditions under which it shall be established and require 
servitudes to be registered in favour of each portion, Erf or unit in favour of the Municipality 
read with the LUM By-law. 
 
(d)   The land use rights on any Property shall be exercised subject to any requirements that 
may be imposed as a condition of title registered for purposes of ensuring that the owners 
of each portion, Erf or unit shall become a member and be bound by the conditions of such 
membership of a non-profit company or any other entity as contemplated in section 34 of 
the LUM By-law. 
 
(e)   Public Street portions/servitudes: 
 
(i)    Where it is the intention of the Owner to provide access via a Property or part of a 
Property which is to be used as a Public Street, the area constituting the Road shall 
be indicated as a Public Street on the layout/subdivision plan of a land development 
or  any  other  relevant  diagram  or  document,  read  with  section  63  of  the  Local 
Government Ordinance, 17 of 1939. 
 
(ii)    The Street shall be constructed free of cost and compensation and to the standard 
and satisfaction of the Municipality. 
 
(iii)   The said portion shall further be transferred to the Municipality, to its satisfaction 
free of cost and compensation read with the LUM By-law. 
 
(iv)   A public right of way may be registered, if and when required by the Municipality, 
and to the satisfaction of the Municipality for access purposes over any Private 
Road/access portion or servitude. 
 
(f)    Restriction on the transfer of sectional title sections/portions of the common property/units: 
 
(i)    The Owner of  a sectional title development shall, at  their own costs and to the 
satisfaction  of  the  Municipality,  design,  provide  and  construct  all  engineering

services including the internal Roads, roadway or road surfaces and the storm water 
reticulation, within the boundaries of the development. 
 
(ii)    Sections/portions of the common property/units in any sectional title development,

transferred into the name of a purchaser, nor a Certificate of Registered Title taken

by and to the satisfaction of the Municipality. Sections and/or units in the sectional 
title  development,  shall  not  receive  an  occupation  certificate  and  may  not  be

engineering  services  have  been  or  will  be  protected  to  the  satisfaction  of  the 
Municipality.  
 
 
CLAUSE 19: GEOLOGICAL CONDITIONS 
 
(1) Development of Property on dolomite ground 
 
For development of all Properties situated on dolomite ground, the Municipality may require one 
or more of the following: 
 
(a)   A dolomite stability and foundation investigation shall be conducted by a qualified person 
acceptable to the Municipality and a report shall be compiled from the results, indicating 
areas suitable for development and specifying conditions under which development may 
take place, in terms of prevailing standards and to the satisfaction of the Municipality, 
before any building operations may commence on the Property. 
 
(b)   Precautionary measures as identified in the report mentioned in Subclause (1)(a) shall be 
incorporated in the Site Development Plans and building plans.  
 
(c)   A registered engineer shall be appointed to establish relevant measures with regard to 
structural work, drainage of the Building and Property as well as the installation of services, 
in accordance with the findings and recommendations made in the report mentioned in 
Subclause (1)(a). The engineer may also be responsible for other measures to minimise 
the dolomite stability risk, as contained in the dolomite stability report, to the discretion of 
the Municipality. A certificate completed by said engineer shall be submitted with building 
plans.  On  the  completion  of  the  development,  the  said  engineer  shall  certify  that  all 
specifications have been complied with. 
 
(d)   A structural footprint or construction report, which is a further refinement of the dolomite 
stability report mentioned in Subclause (1)(a), shall be compiled by a qualified person 
acceptable to the Municipality, in terms of prevailing standards and to the satisfaction of 
the Municipality before transfer or occupation of the Property shall be permitted.  
 
(e)   A dolomite risk management plan, specific to the said development shall be compiled by 
a qualified person acceptable to the Municipality, in terms of prevailing standards and to 
the satisfaction of the Municipality before transfer or occupation of the Property shall be 
permitted. Such plan shall contain an audit report of existing services and structures, where 
applicable. 

 
 
TSHWANE LAND USE SCHEME, 2024 
 
Adopted by virtue of Notice LA 652 of 2024:  08 May 2024  
Comes into operation:  01 July 2024 
                                                                             
 
 
86
 
(2) Development of Property on non-dolomite ground 
 
For development of all Properties situated on non-dolomite ground, the Municipality may require 
one or more of the following: 
 
(a)   A geotechnical investigation shall be conducted by a qualified person acceptable to the 
Municipality and a report shall be compiled from the results indicating the various soils 
classification, in terms of prevailing standards, and to the satisfaction of the Municipality, 
before any building operations may commence on the Property. 
 
(b)   Precautionary measures as identified in the report mentioned in Subclause (2)(a) shall be 
incorporated in the Site Development Plans and building plans.  
 
(c)   A construction report, which is a further refinement of the geotechnical report mentioned 
in Subclause (2)(a), shall be compiled by a qualified person acceptable to the Municipality, 
in terms of prevailing standards and to the satisfaction of the Municipality before transfer 
or occupation of the Property shall be permitted. 
 
(d)   A  registered  engineer  shall  be  appointed  to  design,  specify  and  supervise  structural 
measures for the Structures in accordance with the soil classification as identified in the 
report mentioned in Subclause (2)(a). The engineer may also be held responsible for other 
measures to overcome the detrimental soil conditions, as contained in the geotechnical 
report, to the discretion of the Municipality. A certificate completed by the said engineer 
shall be submitted with building plans. On the completion of the development, the said 
engineer shall certify that all specifications have been complied with. 
 
 
CLAUSE 20: CONDITIONS APPLICABLE TO RESIDENTIAL 1 PROPERTIES 
 
(1) Development controls 
 
(a)   Every Erf has a Density or a Minimum Erf Size that is captured on the Electronic Zoning 
Database  (Schedule  6).  Farm  portions  and  Agricultural  Holdings  with  a  zoning  of 
Residential 1 have no Density or a Minimum Erf Size that is captured on the Electronic 
Zoning Database.   
 
(b)   Where an Annexure L is not applicable, the development controls applicable shall be: 
 
(i)    Clause 25, FAR Zone 21 of Table C; 
 
(ii)    Clause 26, Height Zone 10 of Table D; and 
 
(iii)   Clause 27, Coverage Zone 5 of Table E. 
 
(c)   Where  an  Annexure  L  is  applicable,  the  development  controls  as  set  out  in  such  an 
Annexure L shall prevail, but where the Annexure L has no reference to any particular 
development controls, the development controls of Subclause (b) shall apply. 
 
(2) One (1) Additional Dwelling House 
 
(a)   A Permission in terms of Clause 14(10) for one (1) Additional Dwelling House shall be 
considered by the Municipality, regardless of the Minimum Erf Size or a Density of “One 
Dwelling House per Erf”, provided that, Erven located in the Special Development Areas 
contemplated in Schedules 11 up to and including Schedule 14 shall be excluded. 
 

 
 
TSHWANE LAND USE SCHEME, 2024 
 
Adopted by virtue of Notice LA 652 of 2024:  08 May 2024  
Comes into operation:  01 July 2024 
                                                                             
 
 
87
(b)   Where  one  (1)  Additional  Dwelling  House  has  been  approved  by  means  of  either  a 
Permission or Consent Use and the sizes of the said Dwelling House(s) are restricted in 
square metres (m²), these sizes and related site plan or plan number(s), where applicable, 
shall be disregarded, provided that the Land and Buildings comply with the development 
controls as set out in Subclause (1). 
 
(c)   Where in terms of Schedule IIIB of the erstwhile Pretoria Town-planning Scheme, 1974, 
one (1) Additional Dwelling House which was previously referred to as a “living unit” or a 
“granny flat”, was permitted ancillary to a Dwelling House, as a primary right on or before 
29 April 1992 and it does not reflect on the Electronic Zoning Database, it shall be deemed  
to have been Adopted, provided that: 
 
(i)    the  area  of  such  Additional  Dwelling  House  shall  not  exceed  100 m²  excluding 
Outbuildings; 
 
(ii)    the minimum area of the Erf on which the Dwelling Houses are situated shall be 
1 000 m²; 
 
(iii)   part of the one (1) wall of the Additional Dwelling House shall be a common wall 
with the Dwelling House; 
 
(iv)   the  Land  and  Buildings  comply  with  the  development  controls  as  set  out  in 
Subclause (1); 
 
(v)   the land use rights were exercised; and 
 
(vi)   where an Additional Dwelling House does not comply with Subclauses (i), (ii), (iii) 
(iv) and (v) above, the rights for an Additional Dwelling House shall be regarded as 
not having been granted or Adopted and shall lapse and a Permission as provided 
for in Subclause (2)(a) above shall be submitted. 
 
(d)   Where in terms of Table C, Clauses 17 and 18 of the erstwhile Pretoria Town-planning 
Scheme, 1974, a consent for one (1) Additional Dwelling House that was approved by the 
Municipality after the 29 April 1992 and such approval does not reflect on the Zoning 
Certificate, the Electronic Zoning Database can be updated, provided that: 
 
(i)    the  Municipality’s  electronic  archive  system  known  as  the  CLIPPER  database, 
reflects that an application was submitted, advertised, evaluated and approved to 
the satisfaction of the Municipality. The CLIPPER database consists of a record of 
land development applications submitted, evaluated and approved or refused in the 
jurisdiction  area  of  the  erstwhile  City  Council  of  Pretoria.  This  database  was 
populated in MS-DOS format from a disk drive and the information is only available 
from 29 April 1992 up to dates within the year 2000. 
 
(ii)    the Buildings comply with the development controls as set out in Subclause (1); 
 
(iii)   the land use rights were exercised; and 
 
(iv)   the following further conditions shall be applicable: 
 
(aa)  The provision of engineering services to the Additional Dwelling House shall 
be to the satisfaction of the Municipality. 
 
(bb)  A separate water connection for each Dwelling House shall be provided on 
the Street Boundary. 
 

 
 
TSHWANE LAND USE SCHEME, 2024 
 
Adopted by virtue of Notice LA 652 of 2024:  08 May 2024  
Comes into operation:  01 July 2024 
                                                                             
 
 
88
(cc)   The  Applicant  shall  be  liable  for the payment  of amounts  in  respect  of  a 
contribution towards the provision of engineering services as determined by 
the Municipality. 
 
(dd)  The siting, appearance, design and Height of the Additional Dwelling House 
on the Property shall take the privacy of the existing Dwelling House on the 
Property, as well as the adjacent Properties into account and shall be to the 
satisfaction of the Municipality. 
 
(ee)  The access to the Property shall be to the satisfaction of the Municipality. 
 
(ff)   The driveway(s) on the Property shall be paved or provided with a dust free 
surface to the satisfaction of the Municipality and shall be indicated on the 
building plan. 
 
(gg)  The Applicant shall comply with the requirements and restrictions of any title 
deed, law or by-law applicable to the Property. 
 
(hh)  The consent shall be null and void if the conditions and requirements imposed 
are not complied with. 
 
(3) Subdivision of an Erf 
 
(a)   An Erf may be subdivided only when it has a Minimum Erf Size as indicated in Schedule 6, 
that is the Electronic Zoning Database, or in an Annexure L. 
 
(b)   Where an Erf is zoned Residential 1 and has a Density of "One Dwelling House per Erf" 
as indicated in Schedule 6, that is the Electronic Zoning Database, or an Annexure L then 
such Erf shall not be subdivided, unless stated otherwise in the Annexure L. 
 
(c)   Where a Land Development Application is submitted in terms of the LUM By-law for the 
subdivision of an Erf zoned Residential 1 into two (2) or more Erven (hereafter referred to 
as "resultant Erf or Erven"), such application shall be refused if by that subdivision any 
resultant Erf shall - 
 
(i)    have a size, including the area of a Panhandle or the area of a servitude of right of 
way, if applicable, which is smaller than the Minimum Erf Size as specified in the 
Electronic Zoning Database of the Scheme (Schedule 6) or in an Annexure L; and 
 
(ii)    not have vehicular access to a Street to the satisfaction of the Municipality. 
 
(d)   If  a  resultant  Erf  does  not  comply  with  Subclause (c)(i),  but  will  be  consolidated 
simultaneously with the subdivision of an adjacent Erf with the same development controls 
and  such  consolidation  shall  comply  with  the  prescribed  Minimum  Erf  Size,  then  the 
following will apply: 
 
(i)    such  simultaneous  subdivision  and  consolidation  may  be  considered  by  the 
Municipality; and 
 
(ii)    each  of  the  resultant  Erven  shall  be  subject  to  the  Minimum  Erf  Size  as  was 
applicable  to  the  original  Erf  or  Erven  and  any  consolidation  shall  not  imply  a 
duplication  of  any  land  use  rights  applicable  to  the  Erven  subdivided  and 
consolidated. 
 
(e)   When Land Development Applications for simultaneous subdivision and consolidation of 
multiple Erven are considered and where there are differences in development controls 
and where different Annexures L are applicable, the following shall apply: 

 
 
TSHWANE LAND USE SCHEME, 2024 
 
Adopted by virtue of Notice LA 652 of 2024:  08 May 2024  
Comes into operation:  01 July 2024 
                                                                             
 
 
89
 
(i)    each  subdivided  portion  should  comply  with  its  development  controls  and  split 
zonings shall be added after Adoption, to the Electronic Zoning Database for the 
consolidated Erf; and 
 
(ii)    if each subdivided portion does not comply with its development controls, then such 
application shall be refused. 
 
(f)    If  a  resultant  Erf  is  an  Erf  with  a  Panhandle,  then  the  following  conditions  shall  be 
applicable: 
 
(i)    the Panhandle shall provide access from a Street to the Panhandle Property; 
 
(ii)    the Panhandle shall be not less than three (3) metres wide along its whole length 
and  not  wider  than  eight  (8) metres,  except  with  the  written  Permission  of  the 
Municipality; 
 
(iii)   the area of the Panhandle Property, including the Panhandle, shall be in accordance 
with the Minimum Erf Size requirements, as indicated in Schedule 6; 
 
(iv)   the slope of the Panhandle shall not exceed a ratio of 1:8, provided that it may be 
relaxed with the Permission of the Municipality in special circumstances; 
 
(v)   a Panhandle shall provide access only to the Erf of which it forms a part of, as well 
as the Property in favour of which a servitude of right of way has been registered 
over the Panhandle, except where the Municipality may determine otherwise; 
 
(vi)   the  registered  Owner(s)  of  the  Panhandle  Property  shall  at  their  own  expense 
provide the Panhandle with a dust free surface to the satisfaction of the Municipality 
prior to or simultaneously with the erection of any Building on the Erf and such 
Panhandle shall thereafter be maintained and kept dust free to the satisfaction of 
the Municipality; 
 
(vii)   the  registered  Owner(s)  of  the  Panhandle  Property  shall  when  required  by  the 
Municipality  erect  screen  walls  or  dense  barriers  along  the  boundaries  of  the 
Panhandle  to  the  satisfaction  of  the  Municipality.  The  extent,  material,  design, 
height, position and maintenance of such screen walls or dense barriers shall be to 
the satisfaction of the Municipality; and 
 
(viii)  Buildings shall not be erected in the Panhandle. 
 
(g)   The Municipality may waive the requirement to have a Panhandle to a resultant Erf, on 
condition that: 
 
(i)    a servitude of right of way to a Street, to the satisfaction of the Municipality, be 
registered in favour of such Erf; 
 
(ii)    such servitude shall have a width of not less than three (3) metres and not more 
than eight (8) metres, except with the Permission of the Municipality; and 
 
(iii)   the boundaries of such servitude shall be deemed to be a Side Boundary or Rear 
Boundary of the Erf over which it is registered. 
 
(4) Erven severed by execution of Public Service Infrastructure 
 
Where any part of an Erf zoned Residential 1 is physically severed from such Erf owing to the 
execution of Public Service Infrastructure or Erven to be severed by the proposed execution of 

 
 
TSHWANE LAND USE SCHEME, 2024 
 
Adopted by virtue of Notice LA 652 of 2024:  08 May 2024  
Comes into operation:  01 July 2024 
                                                                             
 
 
90
such infrastructure, the part so severed, shall be deemed to be an existing Erf and a Dwelling 
House may be erected thereon or an existing Dwelling House may be retained thereon, provided 
that: 
 
(a)   the size and shape of such Erf in relation to the surrounding Erven is to the satisfaction of 
the Municipality;  
 
(b)   the Density or Minimum Erf Size of such an Erf shall remain the same in the Electronic 
Zoning Database, provided that where any new Buildings and/or development takes place 
on the Property, the area shall be recalculated to not exceed the land use rights permitted 
and read with section 13 of the LUM By-law; and 
 
(c)   such Erf has access to a Street of which the width is not less than three (3) metres. 
 
(5) Home Enterprise 
 
A Home Enterprise shall be permitted on Properties zoned Residential 1, subject to Schedule 9. 
 
 
CLAUSE 21: CONDITIONS APPLICABLE TO RESIDENTIAL 2 PROPERTIES 
 
(1)   Where an Annexure L is not applicable, the development controls shall be: 
 
(a)   a maximum Density of 25 Dwelling Units per ha; 
 
(b)   Clause 25, FAR Zone 17 of Table C; 
 
(c)   Clause 26, Height Zone 10 of Table D; and 
 
(d)   Clause 27, Coverage Zone 17 of Table E. 
 
(2)   Where an Annexure L is applicable, the development controls as set out in such an Annexure L 
shall prevail, but where the Annexure L has no reference to any particular development controls, 
then the development controls as provided for in Subclause (1) shall apply. 
 
(3)   Clause 31 shall be applicable. 
 
(4)   The following conditions shall be applicable when Dwelling Units are built on a Property:  
 
(a)   Each Dwelling Unit shall have direct access to its own private adjoining outdoor living area 
to the satisfaction of the Municipality. 
 
(b)   That part of the Property between the Building(s) and the Street Boundary which is not 
used for traffic purposes, shall be laid out and maintained as a garden, within a reasonable 
time, at the Owner's cost and to the satisfaction of the Municipality. Should the Owner fail 
to comply herewith, the Municipality is entitled to execute the work at the Owner's cost. 
 
(c)   The  Municipality  shall  not  approve  any  building  plans  which  do  not  comply  with  the 
approved Site Development Plan.  
 
(d)   Subject to the provision of the relevant legislation but notwithstanding any other provision 
contained herein, the Municipality may approve the subdivision of the Property, where 
such subdivision corresponds with the subdivision proposals shown on the approved Site 
Development Plan applicable to the Property, provided that section 34(1)(b) of the LUM 
By-law may apply. 
 
(e)   The provisions of Clause 14(11) shall be applicable to all sectional title development. 

 
 
TSHWANE LAND USE SCHEME, 2024 
 
Adopted by virtue of Notice LA 652 of 2024:  08 May 2024  
Comes into operation:  01 July 2024 
                                                                             
 
 
91
 
(f)    An  individual  Dwelling  Unit  which  is  linked  to  another  Dwelling  Unit  and  ancillary 
Outbuildings shall not be occupied before the relevant Building of which the Dwelling Unit 
forms part is completed, provided that the Municipality may, in exceptional cases, grant 
permission to occupy such Dwelling Unit. 
 
(g)   A Dwelling Unit may not be transferred before the whole development or the phase on the 
Property has been completed, to the satisfaction of the Municipality.  
 
(5)   A Home Enterprise shall be permitted on Properties zoned Residential 2, subject to Schedule 9. 
 
 
CLAUSE 22: CONDITIONS APPLICABLE TO RESIDENTIAL 3 PROPERTIES 
 
(1)   Where an Annexure L is not applicable, the development controls shall be: 
 
(a)   Clause 25, FAR Zone 16 of Table C; 
 
(b)   Clause 26, Height Zone 9 of Table D; 
 
(c)   Clause 27, Coverage Zone 16 of Table E; and 
 
(d)   Dwelling  Units  per  hectare  may  be  specified  only  for  the  purposes  of  calculation  of 
contributions for engineering services. 
 
(2)   Where an Annexure L is applicable, the development controls as set out in such an Annexure L 
shall prevail, but where the Annexure L has no reference to any particular development controls, 
then the development controls as provided in Subclause (1) shall apply. 
 
(3)   Clause 31 shall be applicable. 
 
(4)   The following conditions shall be applicable when Duplex Dwellings or Dwelling Units are built 
on a Property:  
 
(a)   Each Duplex Dwelling or Dwelling Unit shall have direct access to its own private adjoining 
outdoor living area, which area may be a patio on the ground floor or the upper floors in 
accordance with the approved Site Development Plan. 
 
(b)   That portion of the Property between the Building(s) and the Street Boundary, which is not 
used for traffic purposes, shall be laid out and maintained as a garden, within a reasonable 
time, at the Owner's cost and to the satisfaction of the Municipality.  Should the Owner fail 
to comply herewith, the Municipality is entitled to execute the work at the Owner's cost. 
 
(c)   An individual Duplex Dwelling or Dwelling Unit which is linked to another Duplex Dwelling 
or  Dwelling  Unit  and  ancillary  Outbuildings  shall  not  be  occupied  before  the  relevant 
Building of which the Duplex Dwelling or Dwelling Unit forms part, is completed, provided 
that the Municipality may, in exceptional cases, grant permission to occupy such Duplex 
Dwelling or Dwelling Unit. 
 
(d)   Duplex Dwellings or Dwelling Units may not be transferred before the whole development 
or the phase on the Property has been completed, to the satisfaction of the Municipality.  
 
(e)   The  Municipality  shall  not  approve  any  building  plan  which  does  not  comply  with  the 
approved Site Development Plan. 
 
(f)    Subject to the provision of the relevant legislation but notwithstanding any other provision 
contained herein, the Municipality may approve the subdivision of the Property, where

Adopted by virtue of Notice LA 652 of 2024:  08 May 2024

92
such subdivision corresponds with the subdivision proposals shown on the approved Site 
Development Plan applicable to the Property 
 
(g)   The provisions of Clause 14(11) are applicable. 
 
(5)   A Home Enterprise shall be permitted on Properties zoned Residential 3, subject to Schedule 9. 
 
 
CLAUSE 23: CONDITIONS APPLICABLE TO RESIDENTIAL 4 PROPERTIES 
 
(1)   The development controls applicable shall be indicated on the Electronic Zoning Database or in 
an Annexure L. 
 
(2)   Clause 31 shall be applicable. 
 
(3)   Density: 
 
(a)   where Buildings for Apartment Buildings are erected, the number of rooms which may be 
erected on a Property is determined in terms of Condition 1 of Schedule 2 to the Scheme. 
 
(b)   Dwelling  Units  per  hectare  may  be  specified  only  for  the  purposes  of  calculation  of 
contributions for engineering services. 
 
(4)   The provisions of Clause 14(11) are applicable. 
 
(5)   A Home Enterprise shall be permitted on Properties zoned Residential 4, subject to Schedule 9. 
 
 
CLAUSE 24: CONDITIONS APPLICABLE TO A FILLING STATION AND PUBLIC GARAGE 
 
(1)   The development controls applicable shall be indicated on the Electronic Zoning Database or in 
an Annexure L. 
 
(2)   Canopies over fuel pump installations is not regarded as Coverage but shall be considered Gross 
Floor Area (GFA) for FAR. 
 
(3)   Canopies of Filling Stations and Public Garages, excluding the columns, may encroach over the 
Street Building Line by a maximum of three (3) metres. The Municipality may grant Permission 
to relax the projection of the Canopies over the Street Building Line to a further distance than 
three (3) metres read with Clause 10(2). 
 
(4)   Clause 31 shall be applicable. 
 
(5)   Material or equipment of any nature shall not be stored or stacked to a height exceeding the 
height of the screen wall, provided that the Municipality may relax this condition if, in the opinion 
of the Municipality it shall not be detrimental to the general amenity of the neighbourhood.  
 
(6)   Repairs of any nature to vehicles or equipment shall not be carried out, outside the Building, 
except in  an  area which  is screened to the satisfaction  of the Municipality for that purpose, 
provided that the Municipality may relax this condition where the Property is situated within, 
adjacent to or surrounded by industrial uses. 
 
(7)   Material or equipment of any nature shall not be stored or stacked outside the Building except in 
an area which is screened to the satisfaction of the Municipality for that purpose, provided that 
fuel pumps or oil and fuel installations may be sited outside the Building to the satisfaction of the 
Municipality and provided further that the Municipality may relax this condition where the Property 
is situated within, adjacent to or surrounded by industrial uses. 

 
 
TSHWANE LAND USE SCHEME, 2024 
 
Adopted by virtue of Notice LA 652 of 2024:  08 May 2024  
Comes into operation:  01 July 2024

102
 
 
(3) General conditions regarding Height 
 
(a)   The Natural Ground Level shall be used for the measuring of Height, provided that with 
the submission of a Land Development Application, the purpose of which is a township 
establishment application, read with the LUM By-law, the contour lines of the Property shall 
be provided on the layout plan and may be used in the opinion of the Municipality to 
determine the Natural Ground Level of the Property. 
 
(b)   In the event that the Natural Ground Level is already disturbed after the installation of all 
necessary engineering services required to service a township or development area, the 
Existing Ground Level can be determined between two (2) points on the Property, to the 
satisfaction of the Municipality.

(c)   The Average Ground Level shall be determined between the highest corner and the lowest 
corner of the footprint of the Building on the Property. 
 
(d)   The Height of any part of a Building shall be measured vertically from the Average Ground 
Level of the footprint of the Building to the highest point of the Building, as indicated in 
Diagram 1 and Diagram 2.

MULTI LEVEL BUILDINGS ON A SLOPE

Storeys permitted, as indicated in Diagram 3.

104
DIAGRAM 3: GROUND FLOOR/FIRST STOREY  
 
 
 
 
 
(f)    Where  the  Height  of  a  Building  is  specified  in  Storeys  only,  then  a  Storey  shall  be 
equivalent to a maximum Height of 4,5 metres measured from the surface of any floor to 
the surface of the next floor above, or if there is no floor above it, then up to the ceiling. 
 
(g)   Any part of a Building below the Existing Ground Level of which no part is more than one 
(1) metre above such average level, shall constitute a Basement, excluding the floor slab, 
as indicated in Diagram 4. 
 
 
DIAGRAM 4: BASEMENT
