105
 
(h)   Any part of a Building below the Existing Ground Level which is more than one (1) metre 
above  such  Average  Ground  Level  shall  be  regarded  as  a  Storey  as  indicated  in 
Diagram 5. 
 
DIAGRAM 5: STOREY 
 
 
 
 
(i)    In any Land Development Application for the increase in Height, provision shall be made 
for parking in accordance with Clause 28, or as required by the Municipality. 
 
(j)    Where the Height of a double volume Building, is specified in Storeys only, then a Storey 
shall be equivalent to a maximum Height of 4,5 metres measured from the surface of the 
floor to the ceiling above, except where a single Storey Building or the first Storey of a 
multiple Storey Building is designed as a double volume, in which case the Height of such 
Storey shall not be more than six (6) metres, measured from the surface of the floor to 
ceiling, for Buildings for residential purposes and nine (9) metres for Buildings for non-
residential purposes, except with the Permission of the Municipality.  
 
(k)   Where the Height of a double volume Building for Industries, Light Industries, Warehouses 
and Distribution Centres is expressed in Storeys only, then the Height of the Building may 
be equivalent to the total Height of all the permissible Storeys expressed in metres, subject 
to Subclause (3)(h), and the maximum Height of such Building shall exclude the Height of 
the Roof. 
 
(4) Buildings on Properties zoned Industrial 1, Industrial 2 and Commercial  
 
(a)   Buildings on Properties zoned Industrial 1, used for Industries shall not be subject to the 
Height in metres as set out in Tables D and D1. 
 
(b)   The Municipality may grant Permission to increase the Height, where additional Height is 
required for manufacturing and Storage purposes, in respect of any Building, on Properties 
zoned Industrial 2 and Commercial. 
 
(5) Dwelling  Units on  Properties  zoned  Residential  1,  Residential  2,  Agricultural  and 
Undetermined 
 
Dwelling Units on Properties zoned Residential 1, Residential 2, Agricultural and Undetermined, 
shall not exceed ten (10) metres in Height above Natural Ground Level provided that: 

 
 
TSHWANE LAND USE SCHEME, 2024 
 
Adopted by virtue of Notice LA 652 of 2024:  08 May 2024  
Comes into operation:  01 July 2024 
                                                                             
 
 
106
 
(a)   the Municipality may grant Permission to relax the restriction above, if it is satisfied that 
the privacy of the adjacent residents shall not be negatively affected, except where a 
Consent Use is explicitly required in an Annexure L or Consent Use or Permission; and 
 
(b)   the Municipality may grant Permission, that the Height of each Storey may vary from the 
minimum of 2,4 metres as specified in the NBR, or 4,5 metres specified in Subclause (3)(f) 
to a maximum of six (6) metres measured from floor to ceiling depending on the design of 
the Dwelling Unit, except where a Consent Use is explicitly required in an Annexure L or 
Consent Use or Permission.  
 
(6) Exception in the calculation of Height for parking of vehicles 
 
(a)   One (1) or part of one (1) Storey of a Building, used for parking of vehicles shall not be 
considered in the calculation of Height, provided that: 
 
(i)    on Ground Floor an area of not less than 80% of such Storey shall be used for 
parking purposes, the remaining area of 20% may be used for an entrance hall, lifts, 
stairs, facilities for the servicing and maintenance of the Building and amenities for 
the Occupants of the Building and residence for staff necessary for the servicing of 
the Building, but excludes a Caretaker’s Flat, and 
 
(ii)    if the parking storey is on any floor above the Ground Floor, an area of not less than 
85% of such Storey shall be used for parking purposes and access ramps. 
 
(iii)   Dwelling House and Dwelling Units that are not part of a Block of Flats, shall be 
excluded. 
 
(b)   The Municipality may grant Permission for an additional two (2) Storeys used for parking 
of vehicles, except in the area bounded by Justice Mahomed Street, the railway line and 
Steve Biko Street, where only one (1) Storey for the parking of vehicles shall be permitted. 
 
(c)   The exception to the calculation of Height for Storeys in Subclauses (6)(a) and (b) used 
for the parking of vehicles shall be a maximum of three (3) Storeys.   
 
(7) Rooftop antennas or dishes 
 
(a)   Rooftop  antennas  or  dishes  referred  to  as  Private  Infrastructure  Service,  read  with 
paragraph(1)(j) of the definition of Public Service Infrastructure, in terms of Clause 5 of the 
Scheme, may be fixed to any approved Building, provided that: 
 
(i)    the rooftop antenna or dish structures, including the base station, shall not be higher 
than five (5) metres above the Roof of the Building as built, measured from the point 
where it is fixed on the roof to the top of the antenna, as indicated in Diagram 6; 
 
(ii)    the height restriction in Subclause (i) above, applies to the structures and does not 
imply the maximum Height and maximum Storeys as specified in Tables D and D1 
or on an Annexure L or any other Scheme documents; 
 
(iii)   the structure shall not be more than two (2) metres in diameter; and 
 
(iv)   rooftop antennas or dishes that do not comply with Subclauses (i) to (iii) above, shall 
be subject to a Permission before being fixed to a Building. 
 
(b)   rooftop antennas or dishes providing services to the general public read with paragraph 
(1)(j) of the definition of Public Service Infrastructure shall not be permitted on Dwelling

Units on Properties zoned Residential 1, Residential 5, and Special for Residential 1 or

DIAGRAM 6: ROOFTOP ANTENNAS OR DISHES 
 
 
 
 
(8) Increase in Height with the submission of Site Development Plan  
 
The Municipality may grant an increase in Height in any Use Zone, except where it is prohibited 
in  an  Annexure  L,  Consent  Use  and  Permission,  in  accordance  with  an  approved  Site 
Development Plan, subject to Clause 31, in the case of: 
 
(a)   a Building which requires additional Height in order to improve the architectural treatment 
thereof;  
 
(b)   a Building which embodies special features in its design, and that adds to the general 
amenity of the development and area;  
 
(c)   any  part  of  a  Building  above  the  maximum  permitted  Height,  which  is  necessary  for 
maintenance and mechanical equipment such as a lift room and air conditioner units, 
necessary for servicing of the Building; and 
 
(d)   any part of a Building above the maximum permitted Height for the following purposes: 
 
(i)    any chimney, ornamental tower, turret or other similar architectural features; 
 
(ii)    lightning conductor mast; and 
 
(iii)   parapet wall of a flat roof. 
 
(9) Increase in Height with the submission of a Consent Use application 
 
The Municipality may grant Consent Use for an increase in Height in any Use Zone if the existing 
zoning and Scheme documentation refers to the increase in Height by way of a Consent Use 
process or approval, subject to Clause 16.

(3) Exceptions to the permitted Coverage for specific uses as indicated in Tables E and E1 
 
(a)   Coverage for Shop, and Business Building converted to the following, that is Apartment 
Building, Backpackers, Block of Flats and Hotel, shall comply with the following: 
 
(i)    In Coverage Zones 1 and 2 a maximum Coverage of 95% may be permitted for any 
Shop on condition that such Shop shall be adequately ventilated to the satisfaction 
of the Municipality.  
 
(ii)    In Coverage Zones 4, 5, 6 and 8 on Properties zoned Business 1, where Business 
Building  or  Shop  are erected,  additional  Coverage  not exceeding  10%  shall be 
allowed for single-storey garages erected on the same Property for the use of the 
tenants of the Buildings. 
 
(iii)   In Coverage Zones 1, 2, 3 and 4 on Properties zoned Business 1, where existing 
Business Building are converted to Apartment Building, Backpackers, Block of Flats 
and Hotel, the Coverage for such Buildings may be increased with the Permission 
of the Municipality to the maximum Coverage for Business Buildings. 
 
(b)   Coverage for a Place of Amusement 
 
(i)    In Coverage Zones 1 and 2 the permitted Coverage for a Place of Amusement shall 
not exceed 90%, provided that artificial lighting and air-conditioning are installed to 
the satisfaction of the Municipality. 
 

 
 
TSHWANE LAND USE SCHEME, 2024 
 
Adopted by virtue of Notice LA 652 of 2024:  08 May 2024  
Comes into operation:  01 July 2024 
                                                                             
 
 
116
(ii)    In other Coverage Zones the permitted Coverage for a Place of Amusement shall 
not exceed 75%, provided that artificial lighting and air-conditioning are installed the 
satisfaction of the Municipality. 
 
(c)   Coverage for a Building with more than one (1) use 
 
If  a  Building  is  designed for  more  than  one  (1)  use,  the  maximum  percentage of  the 
Property occupied by Buildings at each Storey shall comply with the provisions of Tables 
E and E1 in respect of the use or uses of such Storey. 
 
(d)   Coverage for Apartment Building and Block of Flats 
 
In the case of Apartment Building and Block of Flats being erected on Properties in Height 
Zones 3, 4, 5 and 6: 
 
(i)    a maximum additional Coverage of 15% shall be allowed for single-storey garages 
erected for the use of the tenants of the Buildings; and  
 
(ii)    accommodation  for  employees  necessary  for  servicing  of  the  Building  may  be 
allowed on the top of such garages. 
 
(e)   Coverage for Parking Garages 
 
The Municipality may allow additional Coverage for a Building used solely as a Parking 
Garage, subject to Clause 31. 
 
(4)   Calculation of Coverage 
 
Coverage shall be calculated as defined in Clause 5 and the following Buildings and areas shall 
be excluded from the calculation of Coverage: 
 
(a)   the Basement floor area; 
 
(b)   minor building works as defined in the NBR, up to a maximum of 40 m² for all such minor 
building works on a Property; 
 
(c)   Canopies  or  eaves projections  or  roof  overhangs  up  to  a  maximum  of  one  (1)  metre 
measured horizontally from the exterior wall;  
 
(d)   fire escapes; 
 
(e)   laundry areas and patios (more than 50% open with louvers); 
 
(f)    municipal and other substations; 
 
(g)   eaves projections used exclusively for the maintenance of a Building; 
 
(h)   sun and rain-protection purposes of pedestrians on ground level;  
 
(i)    rubbish-bin rooms;  
 
(j)    Canopies over fuel-pumps at Filling Stations or Public Garages; and 
 
(k)   any car shelter, such as shade netting, with at least three (3) open sides which is not 
included  in  Subclause (3)(b) and  which  is  required  in  terms  of  Tables  F  and  G,  an 
Annexure L, Consent Use or Permission, provided that: 
 

 
 
TSHWANE LAND USE SCHEME, 2024 
 
Adopted by virtue of Notice LA 652 of 2024:  08 May 2024  
Comes into operation:  01 July 2024 
                                                                             
 
 
117
(i)    The number and extent, siting and appearance thereof shall be subject to Clause 31 
excluding Residential 1 and Residential 5; and 
 
(ii)    the Municipality may impose any further conditions it may deem fit. 
 
(5)   Increase in Coverage 
 
(a)   The Municipality may grant Permission for an additional 20% Coverage to be applicable 
on a Property, which shall be calculated as a percentage (%) of the entire area of the 
Property, for any Building in any Use Zone; and 
 
(b)   the Municipality may grant Permission for an increase in Coverage to be applicable on a 
Property, as provided for in an Annexure L or Consent Use.

CLAUSE 29: LOADING REQUIREMENTS 
 
(1) Provision of loading spaces 
 
(a)   Loading spaces shall be provided on the Property in accordance with the sizes in Table H. 
Sufficient  manoeuvring  space,  entrances  to  and  exits  from  the  Property,  internal 
driveways, and, where required, waiting bays, receiving points and turning facilities shall 
be provided on the Property.  
 
(b)   If required, fuelling spaces, with sufficient manoeuvring space, shall also be provided on 
the Property. The number, layout and construction of the loading and fuelling spaces shall 
be to the satisfaction of the Municipality.  
 
(2) Loading and off-loading 
 
(a)   Goods shall only be loaded or off-loaded within the boundaries of the Property unless the 
Municipality has provided loading facilities within the street reserve.  
 
(b)   The condition in Subclause (a) is not applicable to Properties in Use Zones 1 up to and 
including Use Zone 5.

PART 6:  ENVIRONMENTAL AMENITY  
AND APPEARANCE OF BUILDINGS 
 
 
CLAUSE 30: AESTHETIC CONSIDERATIONS 
 
(1) General amenity 
 
Where in the opinion of the Municipality the general amenity of Property in any Use Zone is 
injured by: 
 
(a)   any works of any nature undertaken or proceeded with; or 
 
(b)   any use made of any Building, Property or Land of any nature; or 
 
(c)   the condition of any Building, Property or Land of any nature; or 
 
(d)   any noise, smell, dust or effluent above the norm as determined by the Municipality’s 
Health Officer; 
 
the Municipality may serve a notice on the Owner or Occupant of the Property on which the 
injurious work, use or conditions exist or are being carried out, requiring the Owner or Occupant, 
within a period of twenty-eight days (28) from the date of service of the notice, to take action to 
mitigate/abate and/or make good the aforementioned injurious works, use or conditions and if 
they do not comply with such notice, the Municipality will be entitled to do so on their behalf, or 
have it done on their behalf and to recover the cost thereof from the Owner. 
 
(2) Signs 
 
(a)   Signs and  advertising structures as defined  in the  By-laws for the  Control of  Outdoor 
Advertising, 2006, as may be amended or replaced from time to time, shall not be erected 
on Land and Buildings without the approval of the Municipality in terms of said By-laws. 
 
(b)   Conditions regulating Signs as prescribed in an Annexure L or any Scheme document may 
be relaxed after application is made and approved in terms of the said By-laws. 
 
 
CLAUSE 31: SITE DEVELOPMENT PLAN AND LANDSCAPE DEVELOPMENT PLAN 
 
(1)   The Municipality may require the Owner of any Property intending to erect a Building there on or 
with the submission of an application to submit the following plans in addition to building plans 
required in terms of the NBR: 
 
(a)   A  Site  Development  Plan  and,  if  required,  a  Landscape  Development  Plan  to  the 
satisfaction of the Municipality shall be submitted to the Municipality for approval before 
any  building  plans  are  submitted  or  approved  and  such  Site  Development  Plan  shall 
comply with the following: 
 
(i)    a fully detailed plan to a minimum scale of 1:200, which shall be accompanied by 
means of sketch plans, sections and elevations of all Buildings to a minimum scale 
of  1:100,  provided  that  the  Municipality  may  accept  scales  other  than  the 
aforementioned and which fully illustrates the following aspects: 
 
(aa)  The siting, Height, FAR and Coverage of all Buildings, proposed extensions 
included, and the number of Dwelling Units per hectare. 
 

 
 
TSHWANE LAND USE SCHEME, 2024 
 
Adopted by virtue of Notice LA 652 of 2024:  08 May 2024  
Comes into operation:  01 July 2024 
                                                                             
 
 
125
(bb)  Landscaping,  communal  open  spaces,  recreation  areas  or  children's 
playground subject to Clause 14(11), private living areas, backyards, laundry 
rooms, drying areas for washing, refuse areas, and swimming pool, as well 
as  the  location,  height,  construction  and  finish  of  screen-walls  or  other 
acceptable forms of screening. 
 
(cc)   Entrances to and exits from the Property to any Public Street. 
 
(dd)  The proposed lines of subdivision if the Property is to be subdivided.  
 
(ee)  Entrances to Buildings, Parking Spaces and vehicular and pedestrian traffic 
systems. 
 
(ff)   Street Building Lines, Side Building Lines and Rear Building Lines applicable 
to the Property. 
 
(gg)  The location of existing Buildings on adjoining Properties. 
 
(hh)  Contour  lines  with  0,5 m  or  other  intervals,  or  Height  indications  to  the 
satisfaction of the Municipality. 
 
(jj)    The  grouping  of  Buildings  and  the  phasing  of  the  development  if  it  is 
envisaged not to develop the whole Property simultaneously. 
 
(kk)   The design, Height and finish of all Buildings and Physical Barriers on the 
Property, if required by the Municipality. 
 
(ll)   Precautionary measures to overcome detrimental soil conditions as identified 
in the dolomite stability report.  
 
(mm)  The elevation and architectural treatment of proposed Buildings. 
 
(nn)  Elements such as, privacy of adjacent residential Properties (overlooking, 
balconies and open passages), pedestrian walkways and exterior finish, if 
required by the Municipality. 
 
(ii)    An approved Site Development Plan shall only be amended with the Permission of 
the Municipality. The Municipality shall not approve a building plan which does not 
comply  with  the  proposals  and  conditions  as  set  out  in  the  approved  Site 
Development Plan. 
 
(b)   A Landscape Development Plan, which shall comply with the following: 
 
(i)    A fully detailed plan to a scale of 1:200. 
 
(ii)    The existing natural features and vegetation on the Property shall be indicated. 
 
(iii)   The proposed soft and hard landscape design information shall specify the species, 
quantities and qualities of the plants. 
 
(c)   The landscaping in terms of the Landscape Development Plan shall be completed within 
three (3) months of the completion of the development or any phase thereof. The continued 
maintenance of the landscape development shall be to the satisfaction of the Municipality. 
 
(2)   The  Municipality  shall,  on  submission  of  the  Site  Development  Plan  and/or  Landscape 
Development Plan (hereafter referred to as “the plans”):

Comes into operation:  01 July 2024

(a)   approve the plans; or 
 
(b)   disapprove the plans, having regard to the character and quality of the locality or of the 
existing and/or future Buildings therein, where the proposed Building would, in the opinion 
of the Municipality, detract from the character and quality of the locality, and give notice of 
its decision to the Owner with the particulars and the reasons of such disapproval.  
 
(3)   The Owner of any Property shall not commence the erection of any Building before approval by

and building plan. 
 
(4)   A  Site  Development  Plan  shall  not  be  required  to  be  submitted  for  purposes  of  a  Land

PART 7:  GENERAL CONDITIONS 
 
 
CLAUSE 32: OVERRIDING RIGHTS OF THE MUNICIPALITY  
 
Nothing  in this Scheme shall prevent the erection, use or maintenance of  any Building,  Land and 
execution of works by the Municipality on its own Property. 
 
 
CLAUSE 33: ACCESS AND INSPECTION 
 
(1)   Authorised officials as may be appointed by the Municipality for purposes of enforcement of the 
provisions  of  this  Scheme,  shall  have  the  right  to  enter  into  and  upon  any  Property  at  any 
reasonable time for the purpose of any inspection which the Municipality may deem necessary 
or desirable for the purposes of this Scheme, read with the Act and the LUM By-law. 
 
(2)   Persons shall not in any way obstruct such officials in the execution of their duties. 
 
 
CLAUSE 34: PERUSAL OF SCHEME DOCUMENTS 
 
(1)   The Municipality shall allow any Person to inspect, at any reasonable time, the Scheme, including 
the Clauses, Scheme Maps, Annexures L, Consent Uses and Permissions, in the offices of the 
Municipality. 
 
(2)   Any Person desiring to obtain a copy of such records of the Scheme shall pay to the Municipality, 
such fees as may be determined by the Municipality and the Municipality may provide such 
information by electronic means in circumstances where the copying of such records places an 
unreasonable burden on the officials of the Municipality and unnecessarily takes them away from 
exercising their powers, functions and duties. 
 
 
CLAUSE 35: APPEALS 
 
A Person whose rights are affected by a decision of a Municipal Planning Tribunal or Authorised Official 
on a Land Development Application in terms of the Scheme may appeal in terms of section 20 of the 
LUM By-law, read with the definition of what constitutes a Land Development Application decision as 
contemplated in the LUM By-law. 
 
 
CLAUSE 36: CONTRAVENTION OF THE SCHEME 
 
Any Person or Occupant of any Property, who commits or knowingly permits a contravention of any of 
the provisions of this Scheme or of the requirements of any order or notice issued or conditions imposed 
in terms of this Scheme shall be deemed to be guilty of an offence, read with the Act and the LUM By-
law. 
 
 
CLAUSE 37: SERVING OF NOTICES 
 
(1)   Any order, notice or other document, as contemplated in Clause 36, to be served on any Owner 
or Occupant of Land and Buildings shall be signed by the official of the Municipality, authorised 
to serve such notices, and shall be served in one of the following ways: 
 

 
 
TSHWANE LAND USE SCHEME, 2024 
 
Adopted by virtue of Notice LA 652 of 2024:  08 May 2024  
Comes into operation:  01 July 2024 
                                                                             
 
 
128
(a)   to the said Person personally or to their duly authorised agent or a person contemplated 
in the Criminals Procedures Act, 1977 (Act 51 of 1977); 
 
(b)   by registered post to the Person or their duly authorised agent at their last known address 
or abode, place of business or employment, or post office box number; 
 
(c)   at the domicilium citandi et executandi of the Person to be served; 
 
(d)   by fixing such order, notice or other document on a conspicuous part of the Property if 
there is no such Person on the premises at which service is to be effected; or 
 
(e)   by  electronic  service  in  terms  of  the  Electronic  Communications  and  Transactions 
Act, 2002 (Act 25 of 2002), read with the Act and the LUM By-law. 
 
(2)   Where  any  service  is  affected  in  accordance  with  the  provisions  of  the  preceding 
Subclause (1)(c), such service shall be deemed to have been effected at the time when such 
order,  notice  or other  document would  normally  have  been delivered  and  in  providing such 
service  it shall  be  sufficient  to prove  that  the  order, notice  or  other document  was  properly 
addressed and registered, read with the Act and the LUM By-law. 
 
(3)   Any order, notice or other document required to be served on the Owner or Occupant of any 
Property may be addressed to the “Owner” or “Occupant” without further name or description, 
read with the Act and the LUM By-law. 
 
 
CLAUSE  38:  COMPLIANCE  WITH  TITLE  DEEDS,  DEEDS  OF  GRANT  AND  CONDITIONS  OF 
ESTABLISHMENT 
 
(1)   A Land Development Application approved or adopted by the Municipality in terms of this Scheme 
may not be construed as conferring upon any Person the right to erect or use any Building or to 
use any Land for any purpose which is prohibited in any condition registered against the Title 
Deed or Deed of Grant of the Land, or imposed in respect of the Land under any law relating to 
the establishment of townships. 
 
(2)   The provisions of Clause 14(9) shall apply mutatis mutandis. 
 
 
CLAUSE 39: LIABILITY FOR ERRORS AND OMISSIONS 
 
Adopted land use right(s) recorded in this Scheme read with the general provisions of this Scheme, are 
presumed  to be correct, unless  proven  otherwise  by  an  Applicant.  Nothing contained herein  shall 
prohibit the Municipality from correcting any errors or omissions in the Scheme as contemplated in 
sections 23 and 43 of the LUM By-law. 
 
 
CLAUSE 40: SHORT TITLE AND COMMENCEMENT 
 
(1)   This Scheme shall be known as the Tshwane Land Use Scheme, 2024. 
 
(2)   This Scheme shall come into operation and commence on 01 July 2024. 
  

 
 
TSHWANE LAND USE SCHEME, 2024 
 
Adopted by virtue of Notice LA 652 of 2024:  08 May 2024  
Comes into operation:  01 July 2024 
                                                                             
 
 
129
PART 8:  SCHEDULES 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
SCHEDULE 1 
STREET BUILDING LINES, ACCESS AND PHYSICAL BARRIERS 
 
 
1.    The purpose of this Schedule 1 is to indicate any Street Building Lines, access restrictions and 
Physical Barriers applicable to specific Properties. 
 
 
2.    If a Property is subject to Schedule 1, it shall be indicated on the Zoning Certificate of such a Property 
and the relevant page(s) shall be attached to the Zoning Certificate. 
 
 
3.    Clauses 8 and 9 are applicable. 
 
 
4.    The complete Schedule 1 is available as a separate document on request.

SCHEDULE 2 
FORMULAS 
 
 
1.    FORMULA FOR CALCULATING ROOMS IN APARTMENT BUILDINGS 
 
 
 
The maximum permitted number of rooms in Apartment Buildings shall be determined by the following 
formula: 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
Where: 
 
R    =  maximum permitted number of rooms, and 
 
A    =  area of Property in square metres. 
 
 
 
 
2.    FORMULA FOR CALCULATING THE PROPORTIONAL FLOOR AREA RATIO (FAR) OF A 
BUILDING  
 
 
q  =  
nA +  (nA)²- 4(n-m)AS
 2A
  
 
Where: 
 
q     =  proportional FAR 
m    =  FAR of first use 
n     =  FAR of second use 
A     =  area of Property 
S     =  envisaged floor area of first use, 
 
 
provided that this formula shall be applied to different uses on the same Property and shall not mean a 
spreading of rights from one part of a Property to another part of the same Property in the case of 
different Zonings or different rights on the same Property.

TSHWANE LAND USE SCHEME, 2024

Comes into operation:  01 July 2024 
                                                                             
 
 
131
SCHEDULE 3 
SPECIAL DEVELOPMENT AREA: 
 
HEIGHT RESTRICTION AREA: 
PARTS OF ARCADIA, TREVENNA, SUNNYSIDE AND MUCKLENEUK 
 
 
1.    The purpose of this Schedule 3 is to restrict the Height of Buildings in order to protect and preserve the 
view line towards the Union Buildings situated on Meintjieskop, which is a heritage and political asset of 
the Municipality. 
 
 
2.    Buildings erected on Properties that fall in this Special Development Area bordered and shaded in red 
as shown on the map of Schedule 3 shall not exceed the Height of more than 1 381 metres above 
mean sea level.  
 
 
3.    Relaxation to increase Height that exceeds the metres as specified in the abovementioned Condition 2 
shall not be permitted under any circumstances. 
 
 
4.    Any Land Development Application to relax the Height restriction mentioned in Condition 2, in this Special 
Development Area, shall not be permitted. 
 
 
5.    Any Land Development Application in this Special Development Area, which has the purpose to relax 
or increase the existing permitted Height, as specified on the Electronic Zoning Database, should 
include a certification by a qualified land surveyor that the applied new Height shall be below 
1 381 metres above mean sea level.  
 
 
6.    After completion of a Building, a qualified land surveyor shall certify that the Height of the Building 
complies with the abovementioned Condition 2 before an occupation certificate shall be issued.

SCHEDULE 5 
ADDITIONAL CONDITIONS APPLICABLE TO CERTAIN TOWNSHIPS 
 
 
1.    The purpose of this Schedule 5 is to indicate the list of additional conditions applicable to certain 
townships that were imposed with township establishment.  
 
 
2.    If a Property is subject to Schedule 5, it shall be indicated on the Zoning Certificate of such a Property 
and the relevant page(s) shall be attached to the Zoning Certificate. 
 
 
3.     Clauses 8 and 9 are applicable. 
 
 
4.    The complete Schedule 5 is available as a separate document on request. 
 
 
 
  

 
 
TSHWANE LAND USE SCHEME, 2024 
 
Adopted by virtue of Notice LA 652 of 2024:  08 May 2024  
Comes into operation:  01 July 2024

SCHEDULE 6 
MINIMUM ERF SIZE AND DENSITY OF ERVEN ZONED RESIDENTIAL 1  
 
 
1.    Clause 20 is applicable. 
 
 
2.    Minimum Erf Size and Density are kept up to date on the Electronic Zoning Database. 
 
 
3.    A Zoning Certificate for an Erf zoned Residential 1, shall indicate the relevant Density and/or Minimum 
Erf Size. 
 
 
4.    The information on the Electronic Zoning Database is available electronically and can be provided on 
request. 
 
 
 
  

 
 
TSHWANE LAND USE SCHEME, 2024 
 
Adopted by virtue of Notice LA 652 of 2024:  08 May 2024  
Comes into operation:  01 July 2024

SCHEDULE 7 
METHOD OF CALCULATING NET FLOOR AREA, AND KITCHENETTE 
CONDITIONS GOVERNING THE CALCULATION OF NET FLOOR AREA (NFA)  
OF A BUILDING 
 
 
1. NFA = (GFA - D) (100% - Y) 
 
Where: 
 
(1) "GFA" means the Gross Floor Area of a Building, including, but not limited to, the floor area of 
Mezzanine Floors, and the floor area of Basements, internal passages, the area covered by a 
Canopy over fuel pumps at a Filling Station or Public Garage, external passages and balconies, 
as illustrated by the accompanying Diagrams 7, 8, 9 and 10. 
 
(2) "D" means the sum of - 
 
(a)    the total area of a Building used solely as a Parking Garage; 
 
(b)    the total area of any floor in any Building used for the parking and circulation of vehicles; 
 
(c)    75% of the total area of any arcade, mall or atrium in a Building, provided that such area 
complies with all the requirements relating to health and safety, to the satisfaction of the 
Municipality; or 100% of the total area of any arcade, mall or atrium in a shopping centre 
Building, provided that such area is used exclusively as a pedestrian way; and 
 
(d)    the total floor area of a Building used exclusively as a children's playground as 
contemplated in Clause 14(11). 
 
(3) "Y" represents 5% or such other percentage of the GFA which shall be certified by a quantity 
surveyor or an architect, provided that such percentage - 
 
(a)    is truly and accurately calculated as contemplated by Condition 2 of this Schedule; and 
 
(b)    is acceptable to the Municipality. 
 
 
 
2.    Only the following areas of a Building may be measured and expressed as a percentage for the 
purposes as contemplated in Condition 1(3) hereof, as illustrated by the accompanying Diagrams 7 up 
to and including 12. 
 
(1)    ducts; 
 
(2)    stairs, stairwells, stair-landings, toilets and external passages; 
 
(3)    lift shafts and lift motor-rooms; 
 
(4)    external and internal walls and their finishing; 
 
(5)    fire escapes; 
 
(6)    areas used for mechanical, electrical, electronic equipment, cleaning and maintenance 
equipment; 
 
 
 

 
 
TSHWANE LAND USE SCHEME, 2024 
 
Adopted by virtue of Notice LA 652 of 2024:  08 May 2024  
Comes into operation:  01 July 2024

(7)    projections and architectural features only if they form part of the calculations as per 
Condition 1(1) hereof; 
 
(8)    refuse rooms; 
 
(9)    municipal electricity substations;  
 
(10)   Balconies; and 
 
(11)   such other areas as may be granted with the Permission of the Municipality.

SCHEDULE 8 
NOXIOUS INDUSTRIES 
 
1.    Noxious Industries are subject to Clauses 18(7)(a) and 18(7)(b). 
 
2.    The Municipality may, at its discretion, include any other use, not listed in this Schedule, which in the 
opinion of the Municipality is regarded as a Noxious Industry. 
 
3.    The following uses shall be considered as Noxious Industries: 
 
(1)   LAND OR BUILDINGS USED FOR NOXIOUS PURPOSES: 
(a)   asbestos-processing 
 
(b)   burning of building bricks 
 
(c)   chromium-plating 
 
(d)   cement production 
 
(e)   carbonisation of coal in coke ovens 
 
(f)    charcoal-burning 
 
(g)   converting, reheating, annealing, hardening or carburizing, forging or casting of iron or other metals 
 
(h) 
crushing or screening of stone or slag or plants for the preparation of road-surfacing material, e.g., 
asphalt or tar 
 
(i)    distilling, refining, blending or processing of oils, fossil fuels or fossil oils 
 
(j)    galvanising 
 
(k)   lime- and dolomite-burning 
 
(l)    lead-smelting 
 
(m)   pickling and treatment of metal in acid 
 
(n)   recovery of metal from scrap 
 
(o)   smelting, calcination, sintering or other reduction of ores or minerals 
 
(p)   salt glazing 
 
(q)   sintering of sulphur-bearing materials and viscose works 
 
(r)    extraction of oils or similar liquids/compounds from rubber, synthetic plastics etc. 
 
(s)   Fuel Depot 
 
(2)   LAND OR BUILDINGS USED FOR THE PRODUCTION OR PROCESSING OF THE 
FOLLOWING: 
  
EXCEPTIONS: 
(a) 
carbon bisulphites 
cellulose lacquers 
hot pitch or bitumen 
pyridine 
 
(b)   pulverised fuel Except when used for a spray-painting trade 
(c)   cyanogen or its compounds  

 
 
TSHWANE LAND USE SCHEME, 2024 
 
Adopted by virtue of Notice LA 652 of 2024:  08 May 2024  
Comes into operation:  01 July 2024

SCHEDULE 9 
HOME ENTERPRISE 
 
 
1.    General conditions governing the practice of any Home Enterprise are stipulated in Part A: 
 
 
SCHEDULE 9: HOME ENTERPRISE 
 
PART A: 
 
GENERAL CONDITIONS GOVERNING THE PRACTICE OF ANY HOME ENTERPRISE 
(1) (2) (3) 
CONDITIONS GOVERNING ANY 
HOME ENTERPRISE 
PERMITTED USES FOR A 
HOME ENTERPRISE 
NON-PERMITTED USES FOR A 
HOME ENTERPRISE 
(1) Occupants who reside 
permanently in a Dwelling Unit 
may practise a Home 
Enterprise. 
 
(2) The area and the size of the 
Home Enterprise shall not 
exceed 30% of the Gross Floor 
Area of the Dwelling Unit, 
provided that: 
 
(a) should the 30% calculation 
exceed 60 m², it shall be 
restricted to only 60 m²; and  
 
(b) only be permitted to exceed 
60 m² up to a maximum 30% 
of the Gross Floor Area of 
the Dwelling Unit with the 
Permission of the 
Municipality. 
 
(3) A Home Enterprise shall adhere 
to the following further 
conditions:  
 
(a) The display of one (1) Sign 
showing only the name(s) of 
the Occupants intended in 
condition (1) hereof, the 
address, the telephone 
number, and the nature of

SCHEDULE 9: HOME ENTERPRISE

A maximum of six (6) Persons per class or session shall be allowed,

22:00, or Sundays or public holidays.

148
SCHEDULE 9: HOME ENTERPRISE 
 
PART B:  
 
CONDITIONS GOVERNING SPECIFIC HOME ENTERPRISES 
(1) (2) 
TYPE OF HOME ENTERPRISE: 
LAND USES DEFINED IN 
CLAUSE 5 
FURTHER CONDITIONS GOVERNING THE SPECIFIC HOME 
ENTERPRISE 
(2)    PLACE OF CHILD CARE  
 
 
A maximum of six (6) children shall be allowed, provided that: 
 
(a)    The use shall be restricted to a property zoned Residential 1, 
Agricultural and Undetermined only. 
 
(b)    The health and safety requirements of the Municipality shall be 
complied with. 
 
(c)    No activities shall be held on weekdays after 18:00, or on 
Saturdays, Sundays or public holidays. 
 
(d)    An acoustically acceptable screen wall of at least 1,8 m high, 
shall be erected on the Property boundary, where the children’s 
play area abuts the living-room(s) of an adjoining Dwelling Unit, 
to the satisfaction of the Municipality. 
 
(3)    PLACE OF DAY CARE 
FOR THE AGED 
 
A maximum of six (6) elderly Persons shall be allowed, provided that: 
 
(a)    The use shall be restricted to a property zoned Residential 1, 
Agricultural and Undetermined only. 
 
(b)    The health and safety requirements of the Municipality shall be 
complied with. 
 
(c)    No activities shall be held on weekdays after 18:00, or on 
Saturdays, Sundays or public holidays. 
 
(d)    An acoustically acceptable screen wall of at least 1,8 m high, 
shall be erected on the Property boundary, where the recreation 
area abuts the living-room(s) of an adjoining Dwelling Unit, to the 
satisfaction of the Municipality. 
 
(4)    PLACE OF INSTRUCTION 
 
A maximum of six (6) Persons per class or session shall be allowed, 
provided that: 
 
(a)    The use shall be restricted to a property zoned Residential 1, 
Agricultural and Undetermined only. 
 
(b)    The health and safety requirements of the Municipality shall be 
complied with. 
 
(c)    No activities shall be held on weekdays and Saturdays after 
22:00, or Sundays or public holidays. 
 
(d)    An open air or covered swimming pool used in conjunction with a 
Place of Instruction shall not be included in the 60 m² calculation 
in condition 2(a) of Part A.

SCHEDULE 9: HOME ENTERPRISE 
 
PART B:  
 
CONDITIONS GOVERNING SPECIFIC HOME ENTERPRISES 
(1) (2) 
TYPE OF HOME ENTERPRISE: 
LAND USES DEFINED IN 
CLAUSE 5 
FURTHER CONDITIONS GOVERNING THE SPECIFIC HOME 
ENTERPRISE 
(5)    RETAIL INDUSTRY 
 
(a)    Permitted Retail Industries shall be restricted to the following: 
 
(i)    catering for retail off-site; 
(ii)    confectionery for retail off-site; 
(iii)    dressmaking, sewing of soft furnishing and tailoring; 
(iv)    engraving; 
(v)    electronic requests for printing and copying; 
(vi)    jewellery manufacturing; 
(vii)   photographic processing;  
(viii)   picture framing and screen printing; and 
(ix)    repairing of shoes. 
 
(b)    The following Retail Industries are only permitted with a 
Permission subject to PART A: 
 
(i)    upholstery and window blinds; and 
(ii)    the servicing and repair of audio equipment, air 
conditioners, bicycles, domestic equipment, electronic 
equipment, office equipment, watches and weighing 
machines. 
 
(c)    All other Retail Industries are not permitted under a Home 
Enterprise. 
 
(d)    The health and safety requirements of the Municipality shall be 
complied with. 
 
(6)    SHOP 
 
(a)    Subject to a Consent Use provided that the general conditions as 
set out in PART A shall be complied with. 
 
(b)    A Shop for the exclusive use of online shopping, which means an 
e-shop, where the online administration of purchases is done 
electronically. An e-shop shall be permitted as a Home 
Enterprise without a Land Development Application, provided 
that the general conditions as set out in PART A shall be 
complied with. 
 
(7)    SPAZA SHOP  
 
(a)    Subject to a Permission provided that the general conditions as 
set out in PART A shall be complied with. 
 
(b)    Condition (2) of PART A shall be excluded.

SCHEDULE 10 
SPECIFIC CONDITIONS REGULATING CERTAIN LAND USES 
LISTED IN COLUMN (3) OF TABLE B 
In certain Use Zones of Table B, land uses are listed in Column (3) read with Clause 5 definitions, which are 
subject to certain specific conditions and can only be exercised if these conditions are complied with. 
PRIMARY LAND USE USE ZONE SUBJECT TO THE FOLLOWING CONDITIONS 
1. Light Industry: 
 
(1)    Car Wash  
 
BUSINESS 1 
 
BUSINESS 2 
 
BUSINESS 3 
 
PUBLIC GARAGE  
 
(a)    Provision shall be made for the discharge 
of effluent into the municipal sewer and 
storm water systems to the satisfaction of 
the Municipality. 
 
(b)    Used or polluted water shall not be 
released into the street reserves or the 
storm water drainage system. Provision 
shall be made for such water to be diverted 
to the sewer system in accordance with the 
requirements of the Municipality. 
 
(c)    Noise shall be screened-off to the 
satisfaction of the Municipality. 
 
(d)    A non-transparent screen wall shall be 
erected on the Property boundary(ies) 
adjacent to residential Properties. The 
materials, design, height and finish of the 
screen wall shall be to the satisfaction of 
the Municipality. 
 
(e)    An area for adequate vehicle stacking and 
storage shall be provided in order that 
traffic shall not congest the road. 
 
(f)    Clause 18(7) shall be applicable. 
 
 
 
(2)    Dry-cleaner and carpet-
cleaner  
 
BUSINESS 1 
 
BUSINESS 2 
 
 
(a)    Steam and hot water shall be provided by 
means of electric boilers only, provided that 
the Municipality may grant permission for 
the uses of gas or automatic oil operated 
boilers. 
 
(b)    Provision shall be made for the discharge 
of industrial effluent into the municipal 
sewer and storm water systems to the 
satisfaction of the Municipality. 
 
(c)    Only chemicals of a non-flammable or non-
explosive character as approved by the 
Municipality shall be used in the cleaning 
process.

BUSINESS 2 
 
 
 
(a)    Where the area between the Property

Natural Ground Level of the site, and no

154
 
SCHEDULE 11 
SPECIAL DEVELOPMENT AREA: 
 
MAXIMUM RESIDENTIAL 1 - DENSITIES FOR PARTS OF BROOKLYN, 
GROENKLOOF, WATERKLOOF AND WATERKLOOF RIDGE, AND THE 
CONSERVATION AREAS OF MUCKLENEUK (BAILEY'S) AND WATERKLOOF 
 
1.    One (1) additional Dwelling House in the areas referred to in Condition 2 and captured on the 
Electronic Zoning Database and therefore indicated on a Zoning Certificate of a particular Property 
shall only be allowed subject to the maximum required Density, provided that: 
 
(1)    if there is a Panhandle or servitude area which provides access to the subdivided portion, it shall 
not be taken into account, and  
 
(2)    a Site Development Plan, subject to Clause 31, is required for approval before Building plans 
can be approved. 
 
2.    The following areas are included in this Special Development Area: 
 
 (1)    GROENKLOOF 
 
(a)    A Density of twelve (12) Dwelling Houses per hectare shall be applicable, which means a 
Minimum Erf Size of 833 m² for one (1) Dwelling House. 
 
(b)    The demarcation of this area is indicated on Map 1 of Schedule 11. 
 
(2)    WATERKLOOF/BROOKLYN AREA: 
 
(a)    A Density of ten (10) Dwelling Houses per hectare shall be applicable, which means a 
Minimum Erf Size of 1 000 m² for one (1) Dwelling House.  
 
(b)    The demarcation of this area is indicated on Map 2 of Schedule 11. 
 
 
(3)    WATERKLOOF RIDGE AREA  
 
(a)    A Density of seven (7) Dwelling Houses per hectare shall be applicable, which means a 
Minimum Erf Size of 1 500 m² for one (1) Dwelling House.  
 
(b)    The demarcation of this area is indicated on Map 3 of Schedule 11. 
 
 
(4)    WATERKLOOF CONSERVATION AREA  
 
(a)    A Density of five (5) Dwelling Houses per hectare shall be applicable, which means a 
Minimum Erf Size of 2 000 m² for one (1) Dwelling House.  
 
(b)    The demarcation of this area is indicated on Map 4 of Schedule 11. 
 
 
(5)    MUCKLENEUK (BAILEY'S) CONSERVATION AREA 
 
(a)    A Density of eight (8) Dwelling Houses per hectare shall be applicable, which means a 
Minimum Erf Size of 1 250 m² for one (1) Dwelling House.  
 
(b)    The demarcation of this area is indicated on Map 5 of Schedule 11. 
 
3.    Note: Any rezoning of the abovementioned Properties will override this Schedule 11. 
 

 
 
TSHWANE LAND USE SCHEME, 2024 
 
Adopted by virtue of Notice LA 652 of 2024:  08 May 2024  
Comes into operation:  01 July 2024

GROENKLOOF 5
LUKASRAND

1:4,000
SCHEDULE 11: MAP 5
AREA BOUNDARY
DENSITY:
MUCKLENEUK (BAILEY'S) CONSERVATION AREA
Eight (8) Dwelling Houses per hectare, which means a minimum Erf size of 1 250m² for one Dwelling House. 

 
 
TSHWANE LAND USE SCHEME, 2024 
 
Adopted by virtue of Notice LA 652 of 2024:  08 May 2024  
Comes into operation:  01 July 2024 
                                                                             
 
 
160
SCHEDULE 12 
SPECIAL DEVELOPMENT AREA: 
 
MAXIMUM RESIDENTIAL 1 - DENSITIES FOR PARTS OF 
WATERKLOOF RIDGE AND WATERKLOOF HEIGHTS EXTENSION 3 
 
1.    One (1) additional Dwelling House in the areas (Zones A up to and including E, and Zone G) referred to 
in Condition 2 and captured on the Electronic Zoning Database and therefore indicated on a Zoning 
Certificate of a particular Property shall only be allowed subject to the maximum required Density, 
provided that: 
(1)    if there is a Panhandle or servitude area which provides access to the subdivided portion, it shall 
not be taken into account, and  
(2)    a Site Development Plan, subject to Clause 31, is required for approval before Building plans 
can be approved. 
 
2.    The following areas are included in this Special Development Area: 
 (1)    WATERKLOOF RIDGE - ZONE A 
(a)    A Density of eight (8) Dwelling Houses per hectare shall be applicable, which means a 
Minimum Erf Size of 1 250 m² for one (1) Dwelling House.  
(b)    The demarcation of this area (Zone A) is indicated on Map 1 of Schedule 12. 
 (2)    WATERKLOOF RIDGE - ZONE B 
(a)    A Density of eight (8) Dwelling Houses per hectare shall be applicable, which means a 
Minimum Erf Size of 1 250 m² for one (1) Dwelling House.  
(b)    The demarcation of this area (Zone B) is indicated on Map 2 of Schedule 12. 
 (3)    WATERKLOOF RIDGE - ZONE C 
(a)    A Density of ten (10) Dwelling Houses per hectare shall be applicable, which means a 
Minimum Erf Size of 1 000 m² for one (1) Dwelling House.  
(b)    The demarcation of this area (Zone C) is indicated on Map 3 of Schedule 12. 
 (4)    WATERKLOOF RIDGE - ZONE D 
(a)    A Density of ten (10) Dwelling Houses per hectare shall be applicable, which means a 
Minimum Erf Size of 1 000 m² for one (1) Dwelling House.  
(b)    The demarcation of this area (Zone D) is indicated on Map 4 of Schedule 12. 
 (5)    WATERKLOOF RIDGE - ZONE E 
(a)    A Density of ten (10) Dwelling Houses per hectare shall be applicable, which means a 
Minimum Erf Size of 1 000 m² for one (1) Dwelling House.  
(b)    The demarcation of this area (Zone E) is indicated on Map 5 of Schedule 12. 
 (6)    WATERKLOOF HEIGHTS EXTENSION 3 - ZONE G 
(a)    A Density of ten (10) Dwelling Houses per hectare shall be applicable, which means a 
Minimum Erf Size of 1 000 m² for one (1) Dwelling House.  
(b)    The demarcation of this area (Zone G) is indicated on Map 6 of Schedule 12. 
 
3.    Note: Any rezoning of the abovementioned Properties will override this Schedule 12. 
 

 
 
TSHWANE LAND USE SCHEME, 2024 
 
Adopted by virtue of Notice LA 652 of 2024:  08 May 2024  
Comes into operation:  01 July 2024

TSHWANE LAND USE SCHEME, 2024 
 
Adopted by virtue of Notice LA 652 of 2024:  08 May 2024  
Comes into operation:  01 July 2024 
                                                                             
 
 
167
SCHEDULE 13 
SPECIAL DEVELOPMENT AREA: 
 
MAXIMUM RESIDENTIAL 1 - DENSITIES FOR ERVEN IN 
DEERNESS, RIETONDALE AND RIVIERA 
 
1.    One (1) additional Dwelling House in the areas referred to in Condition 2 and captured on the 
Electronic Zoning Database and therefore indicated on a Zoning Certificate of a particular Property 
shall only be allowed subject to the maximum required Density, provided that: 
 
(1)    a Site Development Plan, subject to Clause 31, is required for approval before Building plans 
can be approved; and 
 
(2)    the Height of the additional Dwelling House shall not be more than two (2) Storeys, provided 
that a second Storey will only be allowed if the Municipality is satisfied that such additional 
Storey will not detrimentally affect the privacy of the adjoining Property Owners. 
 
 
2.    The following areas are included in this Special Development Area: 
 
(1)    DEERNESS 
 
(a)    One (1) additional Dwelling House shall only be allowed on Erven with an Erf size of 
1 400 m² or more, which means a Minimum Erf Size of 700 m² for one (1) Dwelling 
House.  
 
(b)    The demarcation of this area is indicated on Map 1 of Schedule 13. 
 
 
(2)    RIETONDALE 
 
(a)    One (1) additional Dwelling House shall only be allowed on Erven with an Erf size of 
1 400 m² or more, which means a Minimum Erf Size of 700 m² for one (1) Dwelling 
House.  
 
(b)    The demarcation of this area is indicated on Map 2 of Schedule 13. 
 
 
(3)    PART OF RIVIERA 
 
(a)    One (1) additional Dwelling House shall only be allowed on Erven with an Erf size of 
1 400 m² or more, which means a Minimum Erf Size of 700 m² for one (1) Dwelling 
House.  
 
(b)    The demarcation of this area is indicated on Map 3 of Schedule 13. 
 
 
 
3.    Note: Any rezoning of the abovementioned Properties will override this Schedule 13. 
 
 
 

 
 
TSHWANE LAND USE SCHEME, 2024 
 
Adopted by virtue of Notice LA 652 of 2024:  08 May 2024  
Comes into operation:  01 July 2024

ARCADIA 9
ARCADIA 9
LISDOGAN PARK 
SCHEDULE 13: MAP 3
AREA BOUNDARY
DENSITY:
PART OF RIVIERA
One additional Dwelling House shall only be allowed
on Erven with an Erf size of 1 400 m² or more, which
means a minimum Erf size of 700 m² for one 
Dwelling House.
·
1:7,800

 
 
TSHWANE LAND USE SCHEME, 2024 
 
Adopted by virtue of Notice LA 652 of 2024:  08 May 2024  
Comes into operation:  01 July 2024 
                                                                             
 
 
171
 
SCHEDULE 14 
SPECIAL DEVELOPMENT AREA: 
 
MAXIMUM RESIDENTIAL 1 - DENSITIES FOR ERVEN IN 
LYNNWOOD GLEN, LYNNWOOD MANOR, LYNNWOOD PARK AND 
LYNNWOOD RIDGE 
 
1.    One (1) additional Dwelling House in the areas referred to in Condition 2 and captured on the 
Electronic Zoning Database and therefore indicated on a Zoning Certificate of a particular Property 
shall only be allowed subject to the maximum required Density, provided that: 
(1)    if is a Panhandle or servitude area which provides access to the subdivided portion, it shall not 
be taken into account; and 
(2)    the Height of the additional Dwelling House shall not be more than two (2) Storeys, provided 
that a second Storey will only be allowed if the Municipality is satisfied that such additional 
Storey will not detrimentally affect the privacy of the adjoining Property Owners. 
 
 
2.    The following areas are included in this Special Development Area: 
(1)    LYNNWOOD GLEN 
(a)    One (1) additional Dwelling House shall only be allowed on Erven with an Erf size of 
1 400 m² or more, which means a Minimum Erf Size of 700 m² for one (1) Dwelling 
House.  
(b)    The demarcation of this area is indicated on Map 1 of Schedule 14. 
(2)    LYNNWOOD MANOR 
(a)    One (1) additional Dwelling House shall only be allowed on Erven with an Erf size of 
2 000 m² or more, which means a Minimum Erf Size of 1 000 m² for one (1) Dwelling 
House.  
(b)    The demarcation of this area is indicated on Map 2 of Schedule 14. 
(3)    LYNNWOOD RIDGE 
(a)    One (1) additional Dwelling House shall only be allowed on Erven with an Erf size of 
2 000 m² or more, which means a Minimum Erf Size of 1 000 m² for one (1) Dwelling 
House.  
(b)    The demarcation of this area is indicated on Map 3 of Schedule 14. 
(4)    LYNNWOOD PARK 
(a)    One (1) additional Dwelling House shall only be allowed on Erven with an Erf size of 
2 500 m² or more, which means a Minimum Erf Size of 1 250 m² for one (1) Dwelling 
House.  
(b)    The demarcation of this area is indicated on Map 4 of Schedule 14. 
 
 
3.    Note: Any rezoning of the abovementioned Properties will override this Schedule 14. 
 
 

 
 
TSHWANE LAND USE SCHEME, 2024 
 
Adopted by virtue of Notice LA 652 of 2024:  08 May 2024  
Comes into operation:  01 July 2024

One additional Dwelling House shall only be allowedon Erven with an Erf size of 2 500 m² or more, whichmeans a minimum Erf size of 1 250 m² for one Dwelling House.

20   Outdoor advertising Advertisements and/or sign boards shall not be erected or

first being obtained in terms of municipal By-laws for outdoor

Landscape Development Plan 
 
Not required 
22   Geological conditions Clause 19 
 
23   General conditions: 
 
(1) The Occupants of a dwelling unit or residential building may practise, inter alia, their social 
and religious activities and their occupations, professions, or trades, including Retail Trade, 
on the Property on which such dwelling unit or residential building is erected, provided that: 
 
(a)    the dominant use of the Property shall remain residential; 
 
(b)    the occupation, trade or profession or other business shall not be noxious;  
 
(c)    the occupation, trade or profession shall not interfere with the amenity of the 
neighbourhood due to disturbance or pollution through noise, dust, radio-activity, 
gases, fumes or vibrations;  
 
(d)    for the purposes of Retail Trade, a liquor store, and Drive Thru Restaurant shall not be 
permitted; 
 
(e)    a Place of Amusement, Recycling Centre, Scrap Yard and Tavern shall not form part 
of occupations, professions or trades; and 
 
(f)    any waste generated by the occupation, trade or profession or other business, 
especially medical waste, shall comply with the Municipal requirements for the 
temporary storage and removal thereof from the Property. 
 
(2)    In addition to the above conditions the Property and Buildings thereon are further subject to 
the general provisions of the Tshwane Land Use Scheme, 2024.

179
SCHEDULE 16 
CONDITIONS GOVERNING A MUNICIPAL TRANSITIONAL SETTLEMENT 
 
1.    A Municipal Transitional Settlement shall only be established by the Municipality or any Person 
authorised by means of a Council resolution, to do so on behalf of the Municipality, subject to a 
Consent Use in terms of this Scheme. 
 
 
2.    A Municipal Transitional Settlement shall be an area of Land acquired to provide temporary housing for 
Persons identified by the Municipality who are in need of temporary or emergency housing and which 
area of Land shall be formalised in terms of the relevant legislation by the Municipality or any Person 
authorised by means of a Council resolution, to do so on behalf of a Municipality. 
 
 
3.    A Municipal Transitional Settlement shall consist mainly of temporary housing and Streets but may also 
contain Ancillary and Subservient structures and services which in the opinion of the Municipality is 
necessary for the provision of a safe, orderly and healthy living environment. 
 
 
4.    The Municipality or any Person authorised by means of a Council resolution, to do so on behalf of the 
Municipality, shall formalise the area of Land designated as a Municipal Transitional Settlement at its 
earliest convenience and within a reasonable time in pursuance of its responsibilities and legal 
obligations. 
 
 
5.    A Municipal Transitional Settlement shall only be established on national, provincial and Municipal 
owned Property(ies), provided that where Land is made available to an organ of state for purposes of 
establishing a Municipal Transitional Settlement by agreement, transfer of the Property need not have 
taken place before the commencement of an application for a Municipal Transitional Settlement.  
 
 
6.    The process of establishing a Municipal Transitional Settlement shall be read with the provisions of 
section 21 (k) and (l) of the Act and the Municipal Spatial Development Framework of the Municipality 
as it relates to Designated Areas, and all other relevant legislation. 
 
 
7.    The process of establishing a Municipal Transitional Settlement shall include the positive comments 
from the relevant Departments on environmental management. 
 
 
  

 
 
TSHWANE LAND USE SCHEME, 2024 
 
Adopted by virtue of Notice LA 652 of 2024:  08 May 2024  
Comes into operation:  01 July 2024 
                                                                             
 
 
180
SCHEDULE 17 
CONDITIONS GOVERNING MINING 
 
1.    The provisions of the Mineral and Petroleum Resources Development Act, 2002 (Act 28 of 2002) as 
may be amended from time to time and other relevant legislation shall be applicable. 
 
2.    In terms of section 7 of the Minerals Act, 1991 (Act 50 of 1991) as may be amended from time to time, 
prospecting is prohibited in townships, urban areas, Public Roads, railways, Cemeteries, Land used for 
government or public purposes and Land determined by the Municipality in the Government Gazette, 
except with the written consent of the Minister and in accordance with such conditions as may be 
determined by the Minister.  
 
3.    In the event of any conflict between the provisions of this Scheme and any title, right or permit 
contemplated in section 44(4) of the Mining Rights Act, 1986 (Act 20 of 1986), as may be amended 
from time to time, the latter shall prevail. 
 
4.    The holder of a permit for existing Mining rights granted in terms of the Mineral and Petroleum 
Resources and Development Act, 2002 (Act 28 of 2002) before 2 March 2016, may submit a request 
for the correction of errors or omissions, with proof of such permit having been granted on the Property, 
in terms of section 23 of the LUM By-law, which error or omission shall be dealt with in the sole 
discretion of the Municipality and to its satisfaction.  
 
5.    The holder of a permit for Mining rights granted in terms of the Mineral and Petroleum Resources and 
Development Act, 2002 (Act 28 of 2002) after 2 March 2016, shall submit a Land Development 
Application (Consent Use) with the Municipality in terms of Clause 16 of this Scheme, read with section 
16(3) of the LUM By-law. 
 
6.    The mining plan submitted shall be one which has been surveyed and shall contain the necessary co-
ordinates and cadastral information, or such other information the Municipality may require, to be 
identified and recorded on the Electronic Zoning Database of the Municipality. 
 
7.    The Consent Use with reference to Conditions 4 and 5 above so recorded shall lapse when the existing 
Mining rights permit lapses. 
 
8.    Ancillary and Subservient uses such as, housing, recreation club etc. which are required for the 
employees of the mine and which are not required directly in the Mining operation, shall be subject to a 
Land Development Application (township establishment) in the opinion of the Municipality, in terms of 
the LUM By-law or legislation as may be adopted by the Municipality from time to time. 
 
9.    Any further processing of the extracted material or minerals on the Property(ies) of the extraction shall 
be permitted, if in the opinion of the Municipality, it is an integral part of the Mining operations and it is 
not intended for direct distribution and sale to an end user. 
 
10.    Any further processing and crushing of the extracted material or minerals on the Property(ies), not 
deemed to be an integral part of the Mining operations in the opinion of the Municipality, shall comply 
with the provisions of Clause 14 and the specific applicable Use Zone in Table B of the Scheme and 
the applicable Land Development Application in order to legalise these processes on the Property(ies). 
 
  

 
 
TSHWANE LAND USE SCHEME, 2024 
 
Adopted by virtue of Notice LA 652 of 2024:  08 May 2024  
Comes into operation:  01 July 2024

SCHEDULE 18 
CONVERSION TABLES 
 
1. TRANSITIONAL ARRANGEMENTS 
 
Clause 4 is applicable. 
 
 
2.    An electronic - or hard copy of the Conversion Tables forms part of the Guideline as contemplated by 
section 12(3) of the LUM By-law and is available on request. 
 
 
3. SUMMARY 
 
The set of ten (10) Conversion Tables shall include: 
 
Conversion Table 1:  Tshwane Town-planning Scheme, 2008 (revised 2014). 
 
Conversion Table 2:  Akasia-Soshanguve Town-planning Scheme, 1996. 
 
Conversion Table 3:  Centurion Town-planning Scheme, 1992. 
 
Conversion Table 4:  Pretoria Town-planning Scheme, 1974. 
 
Conversion Table 5:  Townships Approved in terms of the Development Facilitation Act, 1995 (Act 67 
of 1995) (Annexure L of this act) or Black Communities Development Act, 1984 (Act 4 of 1984) 
(Annexure F) or other applicable land use legislation such as the Less Formal Township Establishment 
Act, 1991 (Act 113 of 1991). 
 
Conversion Table 6:  Malelane Town-planning Scheme, 1972. 
 
Conversion Table 7:  Peri-Urban Areas Town-planning Scheme, 1975. 
 
Conversion Table 8:  Pretoria Region Town-planning Scheme, 1960. 
 
Conversion Table 9:  Bronkhorstspruit Town-planning Scheme, 1980. 
 
Conversion Table 10:  Greater Cullinan Town-planning Scheme, 1999.
